10056{_}3151{_}At a distance of three or four li from the city, they made a four-wheeled image car, more than thirty cubits high, which looked like the great hall of a monastery moving along.
10056{_}3152{_}The seven precious substances [3] were grandly displayed about it, with silken streamers and canopies hanging all around.
10056{_}3153{_}The chief image stood in the middle of the car, with two Bodhisattvas [4] in attendance on it, while devas were made to follow in waiting, all brilliantly carved in gold and silver, and hanging in the air.
10056{_}3154{_}When the car was a hundred paces from the gate, the king put off his crown of state, changed his dress for a fresh suit, and with bare feet, carrying in his hands flowers and incense, and with two rows of attending followers, went out at the gate to meet the image; and, with his head and face bowed to the ground, he did homage at its feet, and then scattered the flowers and burnt the incense.
10056{_}3155{_}When the image was entering the gate, the queen and the brilliant ladies with her in the gallery above scattered far and wide all kinds of flowers, which floated about and fell promiscuously to the ground.
10056{_}3156{_}In this way everything was done to promote the dignity of the occasion.
10056{_}3157{_}The carriages of the monasteries were all different, and each one had its own day for the procession.
10056{_}3158{_}The ceremony began on the first day of the fourth month, and ended on the fourteenth, after which the king and queen returned to the palace.
10056{_}3159{_}Seven or eight li to the west of the city there is what is called the King's new monastery, the building of which took eighty years, and extended over three reigns.
10056{_}3160{_}It may be two hundred and fifty cubits in height, rich in elegant carving and inlaid work, covered above with gold and silver, and finished throughout with a combination of all the precious substances.
10056{_}3161{_}Behind the tope there has been built a Hall of Buddha, of the utmost magnificence and beauty, the beams, pillars, venetianed doors and windows, being all overlaid with gold-leaf.
10056{_}3162{_}Besides this, the apartments for the monks are imposingly and elegantly decorated, beyond the power of words to express.
10056{_}3163{_}Of whatever things of highest value and preciousness the kings in the six countries on the east of the Ts'ung range of mountains are possessed, they contribute the greater portion to this monastery, using but a small portion of them themselves.
10056{_}3164{_}[Footnote 1: Mahayana is a later form of the Buddhist doctrine, the second phase of its development corresponding to the state of a Bodhisattva, who, being able to transport himself and all mankind to nirvana, may be compared to a huge vehicle.]
10056{_}3165{_}[Footnote 2: A worshipping place, an altar, or temple.]
10056{_}3166{_}[Footnote 3: The Sapta-ratna, gold, silver, lapis lazuli, rock crystal, rubies, diamonds or emeralds, and agate.]
10056{_}3167{_}[Footnote 4: A Bodhisattva is one whose essence has become intelligence; a Being who will in some future birth as a man (not necessarily or usually the next) attain to Buddhahood.
10056{_}3168{_}The name does not include those Buddhas who have not yet attained to parinirvana.
10056{_}3169{_}The symbol of the state is an elephant fording a river.]
10056{_}3170{_}CHAPTER IV  ~Through the Ts'ung Mountains to K'eech-ch'a~   When the processions of images in the fourth month were over, Sang-shao, by himself alone, followed a Tartar who was an earnest follower of the Law, and proceeded towards Ko-phene.
10056{_}3171{_}Fa-hien and the others went forward to the kingdom of Tsze-hoh, which it took them twenty-five days to reach.
10056{_}3172{_}Its king was a strenuous follower of our Law, and had around him more than a thousand monks, mostly students of the mahayana.
10056{_}3173{_}Here the travellers abode fifteen days, and then went south for four days, when they found themselves among the Ts'ung-ling mountains, and reached the country of Yu-hwuy, where they halted and kept their retreat.
10056{_}3174{_}[1] When this was over, they went on among the hills for twenty-five days, and got to K'eeh-ch'a, there rejoining Hwuy-king and his two companions.
10056{_}3175{_}[Footnote 1: This was the retreat already twice mentioned as kept by the pilgrims in the summer, the different phraseology, "quiet rest," without any mention of the season, indicating their approach to India.
10056{_}3176{_}Two, if not three, years had elapsed since they left Ch'ang-gan.
10056{_}3177{_}Are we now with them in 402?]
10056{_}3178{_}CHAPTER V  ~Great Quinquennial Assembly of Monks~   It happened that the king of the country was then holding the pancha parishad; that is, in Chinese, the great quinquennial assembly.
10056{_}3179{_}When this is to be held, the king requests the presence of the Sramans from all quarters of his kingdom.
10056{_}3180{_}They come as if in clouds; and when they are all assembled, their place of session is grandly decorated.
10056{_}3181{_}Silken streamers and canopies are hung out in it, and water-lilies in gold and silver are made and fixed up behind the places where the chief of them are to sit.
10056{_}3182{_}When clean mats have been spread, and they are all seated, the king and his ministers present their offerings according to rule and law.
10056{_}3183{_}The assembly takes place in the first, second, or third month, for the most part in the spring.
10056{_}3184{_}After the king has held the assembly, he further exhorts the ministers to make other and special offerings.
10056{_}3185{_}The doing of this extends over one, two, three, five, or even seven days; and when all is finished, he takes his own riding-horse, saddles, bridles, and waits on him himself, while he makes the noblest and most important minister of the kingdom mount him.
10056{_}3186{_}Then, taking fine white woollen cloth, all sorts of precious things, and articles which the Sramans require, he distributes them among them, uttering vows at the same time along with all his ministers; and when this distribution has taken place, he again redeems whatever he wishes from the monks.
10056{_}3187{_}The country, being among the hills and cold, does not produce the other cereals, and only the wheat gets ripe.
10056{_}3188{_}After the monks have received their annual portion of this, the mornings suddenly show the hoar-frost, and on this account the king always begs the monks to make the wheat ripen [1] before they receive their portion.
10056{_}3189{_}There is in the country a spittoon which belonged to Buddha, made of stone, and in color like his alms-bowl.
10056{_}3190{_}There is also a tooth of Buddha, for which the people have reared a tope, connected with which there are more than a thousand monks and their disciples, all students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3191{_}To the east of these hills the dress of the common people is of coarse materials, as in our country of Ts'in, but here also there were among them the differences of fine woollen cloth and of serge or haircloth.
10056{_}3192{_}The rules observed by the Sramans are remarkable, and too numerous to be mentioned in detail.
10056{_}3193{_}The country is in the midst of the Onion range.
10056{_}3194{_}As you go forward from these mountains, the plants, trees, and fruits are all different from those of the land of Han, excepting only the bamboo, pomegranate, and sugarcane.
10056{_}3195{_}[Footnote 1: Watters calls attention to this as showing that the monks of K'eeh-ch'a had the credit of possessing weather-controlling powers.]
10056{_}3196{_}CHAPTER VI  ~North India--Image of Maitreya Bodhisattva~   From this the travellers went westward towards North India, and after being on the way for a month, they succeeded in getting across and through the range of the Onion mountains.
10056{_}3197{_}The snow rests on them both winter and summer.
10056{_}3198{_}There are also among them venomous dragons, which, when provoked, spit forth poisonous winds, and cause showers of snow and storms of sand and gravel.
10056{_}3199{_}Not one in ten thousand of those who encounter these dangers escapes with his life.
10056{_}3200{_}The people of the country call the range by the name of "The Snow mountains."
10056{_}3201{_}When the travellers had got through them, they were in North India, and immediately on entering its borders, found themselves in a small kingdom called T'oleih, where also there were many monks, all students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3202{_}In this kingdom there was formerly an Arhan, [1] who by his supernatural power took a clever artificer up to the Tushita [2] heaven, to see the height, complexion, and appearance of Maitreya Bodhisattva, [3] and then return and make an image of him in wood.
10056{_}3203{_}First and last, this was done three times, and then the image was completed, eighty cubits in height, and eight cubits at the base from knee to knee of the crossed legs.
10056{_}3204{_}On fast-days it emits an effulgent light.
10056{_}3205{_}The kings of the surrounding countries vie with one another in presenting offerings to it.
10056{_}3206{_}Here it is--to be seen now as of old.
10056{_}3207{_}[Footnote 1: Lo-han, Arhat, Arahat are all designations of the perfected Arya, the disciple who has passed the different stages of the Noble Path, or eightfold excellent way, who has conquered all passions, and is not to be reborn again.
10056{_}3208{_}Arhatship implies possession of certain supernatural powers, and is not to be succeeded by Buddhaship, but implies the fact of the saint having already attained Nirvana.]
10056{_}3209{_}[Footnote 2: Tushita is the fourth Devaloka, where all Bodhisattvas are reborn before finally appearing on earth as Buddha.
10056{_}3210{_}Life lasts in Tushita four thousand years, but twenty-four hours there are equal to four hundred years on earth.]
10056{_}3211{_}[Footnote 3: Maitreya was a Bodhisattva, the principal one, indeed, of Sakyamuni's retinue, but is not counted among the ordinary disciples, nor is anything told of his antecedents.
10056{_}3212{_}It was in the Tushita heaven that Sakyamuni met him and appointed him as his successor, to appear as Buddha after the lapse of five thousand years.
10056{_}3213{_}Maitreya is therefore the expected Messiah of the Buddhists, residing at present in Tushita.]
10056{_}3214{_}CHAPTER VII  ~The Perilous Crossing of the Indus~   The travellers went on to the southwest for fifteen days at the foot of the mountains, and following the course of their range.
10056{_}3215{_}The way was difficult and rugged, running along a bank exceedingly precipitous, which rose up there, a hill-like wall of rock, ten thousand cubits from the base.
10056{_}3216{_}When one approached the edge of it, his eyes became unsteady; and if he wished to go forward in the same direction, there was no place on which he could place his foot; and beneath were the waters of the river called the Indus.
10056{_}3217{_}In former times men had chiselled paths along the rocks, and distributed ladders on the face of them, to the number altogether of seven hundred, at the bottom of which there was a suspension bridge of ropes, by which the river was crossed, its banks being there eighty paces apart.
10056{_}3218{_}The place and arrangements are to be found in the Records of the Nine Interpreters, but neither Chang K'een [1] nor Kan Ying [2] had reached the spot.
10056{_}3219{_}The monks asked Fa-hien if it could be known when the Law of Buddha first went to the east.
10056{_}3220{_}He replied, "When I asked the people of those countries about it, they all said that it had been handed down by their fathers from of old that, after the setting up of the image of Maitreya Bodhisattva, there were Sramans of India who crossed this river, carrying with them Sutras and Books of Discipline.
10056{_}3221{_}Now the image was set up rather more than three hundred years after the Nirvana of Buddha, which may be referred to the reign of king P'ing of the Chow dynasty.
10056{_}3222{_}According to this account we may say that the diffusion of our great doctrines in the East began from the setting up of this image.
10056{_}3223{_}If it had not been through that Maitreya, the great spiritual master who is to be the successor of the Sakya, who could have caused the 'Three Precious Ones,' [3] to be proclaimed so far, and the people of those border lands to know our Law?
10056{_}3224{_}We know of a truth that the opening of the way for such a mysterious propagation is not the work of man; and so the dream of the emperor Ming of Han had its proper cause."
10056{_}3225{_}[Footnote 1: Chang K'een, a minister of the emperor Woo of Han (B.C.
10056{_}3226{_}140-87), is celebrated as the first Chinese who "pierced the void," and penetrated to "the regions of the west," corresponding very much to the present Turkestan.
10056{_}3227{_}Through him, by B.C.
10056{_}3228{_}115, a regular intercourse was established between China and the thirty-six kingdoms or states of that quarter.]
10056{_}3229{_}[Footnote 2: Less is known of Kan Ying than of Chang K'een.
10056{_}3230{_}Being sent in A.D. 88 by his patron Pan Chao on an embassy to the Roman empire, he only got as far as the Caspian sea, and returned to China.
10056{_}3231{_}He extended, however, the knowledge of his countrymen with regard to the western regions.]
10056{_}3232{_}[Footnote 3: "The precious Buddha," "the precious Law," and "the precious Monkhood"; Buddha, Dharma, and Sangha; the whole being equivalent to Buddhism.]
10056{_}3233{_}CHAPTER VIII  ~Woo-chang, or Udyana--Traces of Buddha~   After crossing the river, the travellers immediately came to the kingdom of Woo-chang, which is indeed a part of North India.
10056{_}3234{_}The people all use the language of Central India, "Central India" being what we should call the "Middle Kingdom."
10056{_}3235{_}The food and clothes of the common people are the same as in that Central Kingdom.
10056{_}3236{_}The Law of Buddha is very flourishing in Woo-chang.
10056{_}3237{_}They call the places where the monks stay for a time or reside permanently Sangharamas; and of these there are in all five hundred, the monks being all students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3238{_}When stranger bhikshus [1] arrive at one of them, their wants are supplied for three days, after which they are told to find a resting-place for themselves.
10056{_}3239{_}There is a tradition that when Buddha came to North India, he came at once to this country, and that here he left a print of his foot, which is long or short according to the ideas of the beholder on the subject.
10056{_}3240{_}It exists, and the same thing is true about it, at the present day.
10056{_}3241{_}Here also are still to be seen the rock on which he dried his clothes, and the place where he converted the wicked dragon.
10056{_}3242{_}The rock is fourteen cubits high, and more than twenty broad, with one side of it smooth.
10056{_}3243{_}Hwuy-king, Hwuy-tah, and Tao-ching went on ahead towards the place of Buddha's shadow in the country of Nagara; but Fa-hien and the others remained in Woo-chang, and kept the summer retreat.
10056{_}3244{_}That over, they descended south, and arrived in the country of Soo-ho-to.
10056{_}3245{_}[Footnote 1: Bhikshu is the name for a monk as "living by alms," a mendicant.
10056{_}3246{_}All bhikshus call themselves Sramans.
10056{_}3247{_}Sometimes the two names are used together by our author.]
10056{_}3248{_}CHAPTER IX  ~Soo-ho-to--Legends of Buddha~   In that country also Buddhism is flourishing.
10056{_}3249{_}There is in it the place where Sakra, [1] Ruler of Devas, in a former age, tried the Bodhisattva, by producing a hawk in pursuit of a dove, when the Bodhisattva cut off a piece of his own flesh, and with it ransomed the dove.
10056{_}3250{_}After Buddha had attained to perfect wisdom, and in travelling about with his disciples arrived at this spot, he informed them that this was the place where he ransomed the dove with a piece of his own flesh.
10056{_}3251{_}In this way the people of the country became aware of the fact, and on the spot reared a tope, adorned with layers of gold and silver plates.
10056{_}3252{_}[Footnote 1: Sakra is a common name for the Brahmanic Indra, adopted by Buddhism into the circle of its own great adherents;--it has been said, "because of his popularity."
10056{_}3253{_}He is now the representative of the secular power, the valiant protector of the Buddhist body, but is looked upon as inferior to Sakyamuni, and every Buddhist saint.]
10056{_}3254{_}CHAPTER X  ~Gandhara--Legends of Buddha~   The travellers, going downwards from this towards the east, in five days came to the country of Gandhara, the place where Dharma-vivardhana, the son of Asoka, [1] ruled.
10056{_}3255{_}When Buddha was a Bodhisattva, he gave his eyes also for another man here; and at the spot they have also reared a large tope, adorned with layers of gold and silver plates.
10056{_}3256{_}The people of the country were mostly students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3257{_}[Footnote 1: Asoka is here mentioned for the first time--the Constantine of the Buddhist society, and famous for the number of viharas and topes which he erected.
10056{_}3258{_}He was the grandson of Chandragupta, a rude adventurer, who at one time was a refugee in the camp of Alexander the Great; and within about twenty years afterwards drove the Greeks out of India, having defeated Seleucus, the Greek ruler of the Indus provinces.
10056{_}3259{_}His grandson was converted to Buddhism by the bold and patient demeanor of an Arhat whom he had ordered to be buried alive, and became a most zealous supporter of the new faith.]
10056{_}3260{_}CHAPTER XI  ~Takshasila--Legends--The Four Great Topes~   Seven days' journey from this to the east brought the travellers to the kingdom of Takshasila, which means "the severed head" in the language of China.
10056{_}3261{_}Here, when Buddha was a Bodhisattva, he gave away his head to a man; and from this circumstance the kingdom got its name.
10056{_}3262{_}Going on further for two days to the east, they came to the place where the Bodhisattva threw down his body to feed a starving tigress.
10056{_}3263{_}In these two places also large topes have been built, both adorned with layers of all the precious substances.
10056{_}3264{_}The kings, ministers, and peoples of the kingdoms around vie with one another in making offerings at them.
10056{_}3265{_}The trains of those who come to scatter flowers and light lamps at them never cease.
10056{_}3266{_}The nations of those quarters call those and the other two mentioned before "the four great topes."
10056{_}3267{_}CHAPTER XII  ~Buddha's Alms-bowl--Death of Hwuy-king~   Going southwards from Gandhara, the travellers in four days arrived at the kingdom of Purushapura.
10056{_}3268{_}[1] Formerly, when Buddha was travelling in this country with his disciples, he said to Ananda, [2] "After my pari-nirvana, [3] there will be a king named Kanishka, who shall on this spot build a tope."
10056{_}3269{_}This Kanishka was afterwards born into the world; and once, when he had gone forth to look about him, Sakra, Ruler of Devas, wishing to excite the idea in his mind, assumed the appearance of a little herd-boy, and was making a tope right in the way of the king, who asked what sort of a thing he was making.
10056{_}3270{_}The boy said, "I am making a tope for Buddha."
10056{_}3271{_}The king said, "Very good;" and immediately, right over the boy's tope, he proceeded to rear another, which was more than four hundred cubits high, and adorned with layers of all the precious substances.
10056{_}3272{_}Of all the topes and temples which the travellers saw in their journeyings, there was not one comparable to this in solemn beauty and majestic grandeur.
10056{_}3273{_}There is a current saying that this is the finest tope in Jambudvipa [4].
10056{_}3274{_}When the king's tope was completed, the little tope of the boy came out from its side on the south, rather more than three cubits in height.
10056{_}3275{_}Buddha's alms-bowl is in this country.
10056{_}3276{_}Formerly, a king of Yueeh-she raised a large force and invaded this country, wishing to carry the bowl away.
10056{_}3277{_}Having subdued the kingdom, as he and his captains were sincere believers in the Law of Buddha, and wished to carry off the bowl, they proceeded to present their offerings on a great scale.
10056{_}3278{_}When they had done so to the Three Precious Ones, he made a large elephant be grandly caparisoned, and placed the bowl upon it.
10056{_}3279{_}But the elephant knelt down on the ground, and was unable to go forward.
10056{_}3280{_}Again he caused a four-wheeled wagon to be prepared in which the bowl was put to be conveyed away.
10056{_}3281{_}Eight elephants were then yoked to it, and dragged it with their united strength; but neither were they able to go forward.
10056{_}3282{_}The king knew that the time for an association between himself and the bowl had not yet arrived, and was sad and deeply ashamed of himself.
10056{_}3283{_}Forthwith he built a tope at the place and a monastery, and left a guard to watch the bowl, making all sorts of contributions.
10056{_}3284{_}There may be there more than seven hundred monks.
10056{_}3285{_}When it is near mid-day, they bring out the bowl, and, along with the common people, make their various offerings to it, after which they take their mid-day meal.
10056{_}3286{_}In the evening, at the time of incense, they bring the bowl out again.
10056{_}3287{_}It may contain rather more than two pecks, and is of various colors, black predominating, with the seams that show its fourfold composition distinctly marked.
10056{_}3288{_}Its thickness is about the fifth of an inch, and it has a bright and glossy lustre.
10056{_}3289{_}When poor people throw into it a few flowers, it becomes immediately full, while some very rich people, wishing to make offering of many flowers, might not stop till they had thrown in hundreds, thousands, and myriads of bushels, and yet would not be able to fill it.
10056{_}3290{_}[5]  Pao-yun and Sang-king here merely made their offerings to the alms-bowl, and then resolved to go back.
10056{_}3291{_}Hwuy-king, Hwuy-tah, and Tao-ching had gone on before the rest to Nagara, to make their offerings at the places of Buddha's shadow, tooth, and the flat-bone of his skull.
10056{_}3292{_}There Hwuy-king fell ill, and Tao-ching remained to look after him, while Hwuy-tah came alone to Purushapura, and saw the others, and then he with Pao-yun and Sang-king took their way back to the land of Ts'in.
10056{_}3293{_}Hwuy-king came to his end in the monastery of Buddha's alms-bowl, and on this Fa-hien went forward alone towards the place of the flat-bone of Buddha's skull.
10056{_}3294{_}[6]   [Footnote 1: The modern Peshawur.]
10056{_}3295{_}[Footnote 2: A first cousin of Sakyamuni, and born at the moment when he attained to Buddhaship.
10056{_}3296{_}Under Buddha's teaching, Ananda became an Arhat, and is famous for his strong and accurate memory; and he played an important part at the first council for the formation of the Buddhist canon.
10056{_}3297{_}The friendship between Sakyamuni and Ananda was very close and tender; and it is impossible to read much of what the dying Buddha said to him and of him, as related in the Mahapari-nirvana Sutra, without being moved almost to tears.
10056{_}3298{_}Ananda is to reappear on earth as Buddha in another Kalpa.]
10056{_}3299{_}[Footnote 3: On his attaining to nirvana, Sakyamuni became the Buddha, and had no longer to mourn his being within the circle of transmigration, and could rejoice in an absolute freedom from passion, and a perfect purity.
10056{_}3300{_}Still he continued to live on for forty-five years, till he attained to pari-nirvana, and had done with all the life of sense and society, and had no more exercise of thought.
10056{_}3301{_}He died; but whether he absolutely and entirely ceased to be, in any sense of the word being, it would be difficult to say.
10056{_}3302{_}Probably he himself would not and could not have spoken definitely on the point.
10056{_}3303{_}So far as our use of language is concerned, apart from any assured faith in and hope of immortality, his pari-nirvana was his death.]
10056{_}3304{_}[Footnote 4: Jambudvipa is one of the four great continents of the universe, representing the inhabited world as fancied by the Buddhists, and so-called because it resembles in shape the leaves of the jambu tree.]
10056{_}3305{_}[Footnote 5: Compare the narrative in Luke's Gospel, xxi.
10056{_}3306{_}1-4.]
10056{_}3307{_}[Footnote 6: This story of Hwuy-king's death differs from the account given in chapter xiv.--EDITOR.]
10056{_}3308{_}CHAPTER XIII  ~Festival of Buddha's Skull-bone~   Going west for sixteen yojanas, [1] he came to the city He-lo [2] in the borders of the country of Nagara, where there is the flat-bone of Buddha's skull, deposited in a vihara [3] adorned all over with gold-leaf and the seven sacred substances.
10056{_}3309{_}The king of the country, revering and honoring the bone, and anxious lest it should be stolen away, has selected eight individuals, representing the great families in the kingdom, and committed to each a seal, with which he should seal its shrine and guard the relic.
10056{_}3310{_}At early dawn these eight men come, and after each has inspected his seal, they open the door.
10056{_}3311{_}This done, they wash their hands with scented water and bring out the bone, which they place outside the vihara, on a lofty platform, where it is supported on a round pedestal of the seven precious substances, and covered with a bell of lapis lazuli, both adorned with rows of pearls.
10056{_}3312{_}Its color is of a yellowish white, and it forms an imperfect circle twelve inches round, curving upwards to the centre.
10056{_}3313{_}Every day, after it has been brought forth, the keepers of the vihara ascend a high gallery, where they beat great drums, blow conches, and clash their copper cymbals.
10056{_}3314{_}When the king hears them, he goes to the vihara, and makes his offerings of flowers and incense.
10056{_}3315{_}When he has done this, he and his attendants in order, one after another, raise the bone, place it for a moment on the top of their heads, and then depart, going out by the door on the west as they had entered by that on the east.
10056{_}3316{_}The king every morning makes his offerings and performs his worship, and afterwards gives audience on the business of his government.
10056{_}3317{_}The chiefs of the Vaisyas [4] also make their offerings before they attend to their family affairs.
10056{_}3318{_}Every day it is so, and there is no remissness in the observance of the custom.
10056{_}3319{_}When all of the offerings are over, they replace the bone in the vihara, where there is a vimoksha tope, of the seven precious substances, and rather more than five cubits high, sometimes open, sometimes shut, to contain it.
10056{_}3320{_}In front of the door of the vihara, there are parties who every morning sell flowers and incense, and those who wish to make offerings buy some of all kinds.
10056{_}3321{_}The kings of various countries are also constantly sending messengers with offerings.
10056{_}3322{_}The vihara stands in a square of thirty paces, and though heaven should shake and earth be rent, this place would not move.
10056{_}3323{_}Going on, north from this, for a yojana, Fa-hien arrived at the capital of Nagara, the place where the Bodhisattva once purchased with money five stalks of flowers, as an offering to the Dipankara Buddha.
10056{_}3324{_}In the midst of the city there is also the tope of Buddha's tooth, where offerings are made in the same way as to the flat-bone of his skull.
10056{_}3325{_}A yojana to the northeast of the city brought him to the mouth of a valley, where there is Buddha's pewter staff; and a vihara also has been built at which offerings are made.
10056{_}3326{_}The staff is made of Gosirsha Chandana, and is quite sixteen or seventeen cubits long.
10056{_}3327{_}It is contained in a wooden tube, and though a hundred or a thousand men were to try to lift it, they could not move it.
10056{_}3328{_}Entering the mouth of the valley, and going west, he found Buddha's Sanghali, [5] where also there is reared a vihara, and offerings are made.
10056{_}3329{_}It is a custom of the country when there is a great drought, for the people to collect in crowds, bring out the robe, pay worship to it, and make offerings, on which there is immediately a great rain from the sky.
10056{_}3330{_}South of the city, half a yojana, there is a rock-cavern, in a great hill fronting the southwest; and here it was that Buddha left his shadow.
10056{_}3331{_}Looking at it from a distance of more than ten paces, you seem to see Buddha's real form, with his complexion of gold, and his characteristic marks in their nicety, clearly and brightly displayed.
10056{_}3332{_}The nearer you approach, however, the fainter it becomes, as if it were only in your fancy.
10056{_}3333{_}When the kings from the regions all around have sent skilful artists to take a copy, none of them have been able to do so.
10056{_}3334{_}Among the people of the country there is a saying current that "the thousand Buddhas must all leave their shadows here."
10056{_}3335{_}Rather more than four hundred paces west from the shadow, when Buddha was at the spot, he shaved off his hair and clipped his nails, and proceeded, along with his disciples, to build a tope seventy or eighty cubits high, to be a model for all future topes; and it is still existing.
10056{_}3336{_}By the side of it there is a monastery, with more than seven hundred monks in it.
10056{_}3337{_}At this place there are as many as a thousand topes of Arhans and Pratyeka Buddhas.
10056{_}3338{_}[Footnote 1: Now in India, Fa-hien used the Indian measure of distance; but it is not possible to determine exactly what its length then was.
10056{_}3339{_}The estimates of it are very different, and vary from four and a half or five miles to seven, and sometimes more.]
10056{_}3340{_}[Footnote 2: The present Hidda, west of Peshawur, and five miles south of Jellalabad.]
10056{_}3341{_}[Footnote 3: "The vihara," says Hardy, "is the residence of a recluse or priest;" and so Davids--"the clean little hut where the mendicant lives."]
10056{_}3342{_}[Footnote 4: The Vaisyas, or the bourgeois caste of Hindu society, are described here as "resident scholars."]
10056{_}3343{_}[Footnote 5: Or Sanghati, the double or composite robe, part of a monk's attire, reaching from the shoulders to the knees, and fastened round the waist.]
10056{_}3344{_}CHAPTER XIV  ~Crossing the Indus to the East~   Having stayed there till the third month of winter, Fa-hien and the two others, proceeding southwards, crossed the Little Snowy mountains.
10056{_}3345{_}On them the snow lies accumulated both winter and summer.
10056{_}3346{_}On the north side of the mountains, in the shade, they suddenly encountered a cold wind which made them shiver and become unable to speak.
10056{_}3347{_}Hwuy-king could not go any farther.
10056{_}3348{_}A white froth came from his mouth, and he said to Fa-hien, "I cannot live any longer.
10056{_}3349{_}Do you immediately go away, that we do not all die here"; and with these words he died.
10056{_}3350{_}Fa-hien stroked the corpse, and cried out piteously, "Our original plan has failed; it is fate.
10056{_}3351{_}What can we do?"
10056{_}3352{_}He then again exerted himself, and they succeeded in crossing to the south of the range, and arrived in the kingdom of Lo-e, [1] where there were nearly three thousand monks, students of both the mahayana and hinayana.
10056{_}3353{_}Here they stayed for the summer retreat, [2] and when that was over, they went on to the south, and ten days' journey brought them to the kingdom of Poh-na, where there are also more than three thousand monks, all students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3354{_}Proceeding from this place for three days, they again crossed the Indus, where the country on each side was low and level.
10056{_}3355{_}[Footnote 1: Lo-e, or Rohi, or Afghanistan; only a portion of it can be intended.]
10056{_}3356{_}[Footnote 2: We are now therefore in A.D.
10056{_}3357{_}404.]
10056{_}3358{_}CHAPTER XV  ~Sympathy of Monks with the Pilgrims~   After they had crossed the river, there was a country named Pe-t'oo, where Buddhism was very flourishing, and the monks studied both the mahayana and hinayana.
10056{_}3359{_}When they saw their fellow-disciples from Ts'in passing along, they were moved with great pity and sympathy, and expressed themselves thus: "How is it that these men from a border-land should have learned to become monks, and come for the sake of our doctrines from such a distance in search of the Law of Buddha?"
10056{_}3360{_}They supplied them with what they needed, and treated them in accordance with the rules of the Law.
10056{_}3361{_}CHAPTER XVI  ~Condition and Customs of Central India~   From this place they travelled southeast, passing by a succession of very many monasteries, with a multitude of monks, who might be counted by myriads.
10056{_}3362{_}After passing all these places, they came to a country named Ma-t'aou-lo.
10056{_}3363{_}They still followed the course of the P'oo-na river, on the banks of which, left and right, there were twenty monasteries, which might contain three thousand monks; and here the Law of Buddha was still more flourishing.
10056{_}3364{_}Everywhere, from the Sandy Desert, in all the countries of India, the kings had been firm believers in that Law.
10056{_}3365{_}When they make their offerings to a community of monks, they take off their royal caps, and along with their relatives and ministers, supply them with food with their own hands.
10056{_}3366{_}That done, the king has a carpet spread for himself on the ground, and sits down on it in front of the chairman;--they dare not presume to sit on couches in front of the community.
10056{_}3367{_}The laws and ways, according to which the kings presented their offerings when Buddha was in the world, have been handed down to the present day.
10056{_}3368{_}All south from this is named the Middle Kingdom.
10056{_}3369{_}In it the cold and heat are finely tempered, and there is neither hoarfrost nor snow.
10056{_}3370{_}The people are numerous and happy; they have not to register their households, or attend to any magistrates and their rules; only those who cultivate the royal land have to pay a portion of the gain from it.
10056{_}3371{_}If they want to go they go; if they want to stay on, they stay.
10056{_}3372{_}The king governs without decapitation or other corporal punishments.
10056{_}3373{_}Criminals are simply fined, lightly or heavily, according to the circumstances of each case.
10056{_}3374{_}Even in cases of repeated attempts at wicked rebellion, they only have their right hands cut off.
10056{_}3375{_}The king's body-guards and attendants all have salaries.
10056{_}3376{_}Throughout the whole country the people do not kill any living creature, nor drink intoxicating liquor, nor eat onions or garlic.
10056{_}3377{_}The only exception is that of the Chandalas.
10056{_}3378{_}That is the name for those who are held to be wicked men, and live apart from others.
10056{_}3379{_}When they enter the gate of a city or a market-place, they strike a piece of wood to make themselves known, so that men know and avoid them, and do not come into contact with them.
10056{_}3380{_}In that country they do not keep pigs and fowls, and do not sell live cattle; in the markets there are no butchers' shops and no dealers in intoxicating drink.
10056{_}3381{_}In buying and selling commodities they use cowries.
10056{_}3382{_}Only the Chandalas are fishermen and hunters, and sell flesh meat.
10056{_}3383{_}After Buddha attained to pari-nirvana the kings of the various countries and the heads of the Vaisyas built viharas for the priests, and endowed them with fields, houses, gardens, and orchards, along with the resident populations and their cattle, the grants being engraved on plates of metal, so that afterwards they were handed down from king to king, without any one daring to annul them, and they remain even to the present time.
10056{_}3384{_}The regular business of the monks is to perform acts of meritorious virtue, and to recite their Sutras and sit wrapped in meditation.
10056{_}3385{_}When stranger monks arrive at any monastery, the old residents meet and receive them, carry for them their clothes and alms-bowl, give them water to wash their feet, oil with which to anoint them, and the liquid food permitted out of the regular hours.
10056{_}3386{_}[1] When the stranger has enjoyed a very brief rest, they further ask the number of years that he has been a monk, after which he receives a sleeping apartment with its appurtenances, according to his regular order, and everything is done for him which the rules prescribe.
10056{_}3387{_}Where a community of monks resides, they erect topes to Sariputtra, [2] to Maha-maudgalyayana, [3] and to Ananda, and also topes in honor of the Abhidharma, [4] the Vinaya, [4] and the Sutras.
10056{_}3388{_}[4] A month after the annual season of rest, the families which are looking out for blessing stimulate one another to make offerings to the monks, and send round to them the liquid food which may be taken out of the ordinary hours.
10056{_}3389{_}All the monks come together in a great assembly, and preach the Law; after which offerings are presented at the tope of Sariputtra, with all kinds of flowers and incense.
10056{_}3390{_}All through the night lamps are kept burning, and skilful musicians are employed to perform.
10056{_}3391{_}When Sariputtra was a great Brahman, he went to Buddha, and begged to be permitted to quit his family and become a monk.
10056{_}3392{_}The great Mugalan and the great Kas'yapa also did the same.
10056{_}3393{_}The bhikshunis [5] for the most part make their offerings at the tope of Ananda, because it was he who requested the World-honored one to allow females to quit their families and become nuns.
10056{_}3394{_}The Sramaneras [6] mostly make their offerings to Rahula.
10056{_}3395{_}[7] The professors of the Abhidharma make their offerings to it; those of the Vinaya to it.
10056{_}3396{_}Every year there is one such offering, and each class has its own day for it.
10056{_}3397{_}Students of the mahayana present offerings to the Prajna-paramita, to Manjus'ri, and to Kwan-she-yin.
10056{_}3398{_}When the monks have done receiving their annual tribute from the harvests, the Heads of the Vaisyas and all the Brahmans bring clothes and such other articles as the monks require for use, and distribute among them.
10056{_}3399{_}The monks, having received them, also proceed to give portions to one another.
10056{_}3400{_}From the nirvana of Buddha, the forms of ceremony, laws, and rules, practised by the sacred communities, have been handed down from one generation to another without interruption.
10056{_}3401{_}From the place where the travellers crossed the Indus to South India, and on to the Southern Sea, a distance of forty or fifty thousand li, all is level plain.
10056{_}3402{_}There are no large hills with streams among them; there are simply the waters of the rivers.
10056{_}3403{_}[Footnote 1: No monk can eat solid food except between sunrise and noon, and total abstinence from intoxicating drinks is obligatory.
10056{_}3404{_}Food eaten at any other part of the day is called vikala, and forbidden; but a weary traveller might receive unseasonable refreshment, consisting of honey, butter, treacle, and sesamum oil.]
10056{_}3405{_}[Footnote 2: Sariputtra was one of the principal disciples of Buddha, and indeed the most learned and ingenious of them all.]
10056{_}3406{_}[Footnote 3: Mugalan, the Singhalese name of this disciple, is more pronounceable.
10056{_}3407{_}He also was one of the principal disciples, called Buddha's "left-hand attendant."
10056{_}3408{_}He was distinguished for his power of vision, and his magic powers.]
10056{_}3409{_}[Footnote 4: The different parts of the tripitaka.]
10056{_}3410{_}[Footnote 5: The bhikshunis are the female monks or nuns, subject to the same rules as the bhikshus, and also to special ordinances of restraint.]
10056{_}3411{_}[Footnote 6: The Sramaneras are the novices, male or female, who have vowed to observe the Shikshapada, or ten commandments.]
10056{_}3412{_}[Footnote 7: The eldest son of Sakyamuni by Yasodhara.
10056{_}3413{_}Converted to Buddhism, he followed his father as an attendant; and after Buddha's death became the founder of a philosophical realistic school (vaibhashika).
10056{_}3414{_}He is now revered as the patron saint of all novices, and is to be reborn as the eldest son of every future Buddha.]
10056{_}3415{_}CHAPTER XVII  ~Legend of the Trayastrimsas Heaven~   From this they proceeded southeast for eighteen yojanas, and found themselves in a kingdom called Sankas'ya, at the place where Buddha came down, after ascending to the Trayastrims'as heaven [1], and there preaching for three months his Law for the benefit of his mother [2].
10056{_}3416{_}Buddha had gone up to this heaven by his supernatural power, without letting his disciples know; but seven days before the completion of the three months he laid aside his invisibility, and Anuruddha [3], with his heavenly eyes, saw the World-honored one, and immediately said to the honored one, the great Mugalan, "Do you go and salute the World-honored one," Mugalan forthwith went, and with head and face did homage at Buddha's feet.
10056{_}3417{_}They then saluted and questioned each other, and when this was over, Buddha said to Mugalan, "Seven days after this I will go down to Jambudvipa"; and thereupon Mugalan returned.
10056{_}3418{_}At this time the great kings of eight countries with their ministers and people, not having seen Buddha for a long time, were all thirstily looking up for him, and had collected in clouds in this kingdom to wait for the World-honored one.
10056{_}3419{_}Then the bhikshuni Utpala thought in her heart, "To-day the kings, with their ministers and people, will all be meeting and welcoming Buddha.
10056{_}3420{_}I am but a woman; how shall I succeed in being the first to see him?"
10056{_}3421{_}Buddha immediately, by his spirit-like power, changed her into the appearance of a holy Chakravartti king, and she was the foremost of all in doing reverence to him.
10056{_}3422{_}As Buddha descended from his position aloft in the Trayastrims'as heaven, when he was coming down, there were made to appear three flights of precious steps.
10056{_}3423{_}Buddha was on the middle flight, the steps of which were composed of the seven precious substances.
10056{_}3424{_}The king of Brahma-loka [4] also made a flight of silver steps appear on the right side, where he was seen attending with a white chowry in his hand.
10056{_}3425{_}Sakra, Ruler of Devas, made a flight of steps of purple gold on the left side, where he was seen attending and holding an umbrella of the seven precious substances.
10056{_}3426{_}An innumerable multitude of the devas followed Buddha in his descent.
10056{_}3427{_}When he was come down, the three flights all disappeared in the ground, excepting seven steps, which continued to be visible.
10056{_}3428{_}Afterwards king As'oka, wishing to know where their ends rested, sent men to dig and see.
10056{_}3429{_}They went down to the yellow springs without reaching the bottom of the steps, and from this the king received an increase to his reverence and faith, and built a vihara over the steps, with a standing image, sixteen cubits in height, right over the middle flight.
10056{_}3430{_}Behind the vihara he erected a stone pillar, about fifty cubits high, with a lion on the top of it.
10056{_}3431{_}[5] Let into the pillar, on each of its four sides, there is an image of Buddha, inside and out shining and transparent, and pure as it were of lapis lazuli.
10056{_}3432{_}Some teachers of another doctrine once disputed with the S'ramanas about the right to this as a place of residence, and the latter were having the worst of the argument, when they took an oath on both sides on the condition that, if the place did indeed belong to the S'ramanas, there should be some marvellous attestation of it.
10056{_}3433{_}When these words had been spoken, the lion on the top gave a great roar, thus giving the proof; on which their opponents were frightened, bowed to the decision, and withdrew.
10056{_}3434{_}Through Buddha having for three months partaken of the food of heaven, his body emitted a heavenly fragrance, unlike that of an ordinary man.
10056{_}3435{_}He went immediately and bathed; and afterwards, at the spot where he did so, a bathing-house was built, which is still existing.
10056{_}3436{_}At the place where the bhikshuni Utpala was the first to do reverence to Buddha, a tope has now been built.
10056{_}3437{_}At the places where Buddha, when he was in the world, cut his hair and nails, topes are erected; and where the three Buddhas [6] that preceded S'akyamuni Buddha and he himself sat; where they walked, and where images of their persons were made.
10056{_}3438{_}At all these places topes were made, and are still existing.
10056{_}3439{_}At the place where S'akra, Ruler of the Devas, and the king of the Brahma-loka followed Buddha down from the Trayastrimsas heaven they have also raised a tope.
10056{_}3440{_}At this place the monks and nuns may be a thousand, who all receive their food from the common store, and pursue their studies, some of the mahayana and some of the hinayana.
10056{_}3441{_}Where they live, there is a white-eared dragon, which acts the part of danapati to the community of these monks, causing abundant harvests in the country, and the enriching rains to come in season, without the occurrence of any calamities, so that the monks enjoy their repose and ease.
10056{_}3442{_}In gratitude for its kindness, they have made for it a dragon-house, with a carpet for it to sit on, and appointed for it a diet of blessing, which they present for its nourishment.
10056{_}3443{_}Every day they set apart three of their number to go to its house, and eat there.
10056{_}3444{_}Whenever the summer retreat is ended, the dragon straightway changes its form, and appears as a small snake, with white spots at the side of its ears.
10056{_}3445{_}As soon as the monks recognize it, they fill a copper vessel with cream, into which they put the creature, and then carry it round from the one who has the highest seat at their tables to him who has the lowest, when it appears as if saluting them.
10056{_}3446{_}When it has been taken round, immediately it disappears; and every year it thus comes forth once.
10056{_}3447{_}The country is very productive, and the people are prosperous, and happy beyond comparison.
10056{_}3448{_}When people of other countries come to it, they are exceedingly attentive to them all, and supply them with what they need.
10056{_}3449{_}Fifty yojanas northwest from the monastery there is another, called "The Great Heap."
10056{_}3450{_}Great Heap was the name of a wicked demon, who was converted by Buddha, and men subsequently at this place reared a vihara.
10056{_}3451{_}When it was being made over to an Arhat by pouring water on his hands, some drops fell on the ground.
10056{_}3452{_}They are still on the spot, and however they may be brushed away and removed, they continue to be visible, and cannot be made to disappear.
10056{_}3453{_}At this place there is also a tope to Buddha, where a good spirit constantly keeps all about it swept and watered, without any labor of man being required.
10056{_}3454{_}A king of corrupt views once said, "Since you are able to do this, I will lead a multitude of troops and reside there till the dirt and filth has increased and accumulated, and see whether you can cleanse it away or not."
10056{_}3455{_}The spirit thereupon raised a great wind, which blew the filth away, and made the place pure.
10056{_}3456{_}At this place there are many small topes, at which a man may keep counting a whole day without being able to know their exact number.
10056{_}3457{_}If he be firmly bent on knowing it, he will place a man by the side of each tope.
10056{_}3458{_}When this is done, proceeding to count the number of the men, whether they be many or few, he will not get to know the number.
10056{_}3459{_}[7]  There is a monastery, containing perhaps six hundred or seven hundred monks, in which there is a place where a Pratyeka Buddha used to take his food.
10056{_}3460{_}The nirvana ground where he was burned after death is as large as a carriage wheel; and while grass grows all around, on this spot there is none.
10056{_}3461{_}The ground also where he dried his clothes produces no grass, but the impression of them, where they lay on it, continues to the present day.
10056{_}3462{_}[Footnote 1: The heaven of Indra or Sakya, meaning "the heaven of thirty-three classes," a name which has been explained both historically and mythologically.
10056{_}3463{_}"The description of it," says Eitel, "tallies in all respects with the Svarga of Brahmanic mythology.
10056{_}3464{_}It is situated between the four peaks of the Meru, and consists of thirty-two cities of devas, eight on each of the four corners of the mountain.
10056{_}3465{_}Indra's capital of Bellevue is in the centre.
10056{_}3466{_}There he is enthroned, with a thousand heads and a thousand eyes, and four arms grasping the vajra, with his wife and 119,000 concubines.
10056{_}3467{_}There he receives the monthly reports of the four Maharajas, concerning the progress of good and evil in the world," etc., etc.]
10056{_}3468{_}[Footnote 2: Buddha's mother, Maya and Maha-maya, died seven days after his birth.]
10056{_}3469{_}[Footnote 3: Anuruddha was a first cousin of Sakyamuni, being the son of his uncle Amritodana.
10056{_}3470{_}He is often mentioned in the account we have of Buddha's last moments.
10056{_}3471{_}His special gift was the "heavenly eye," the first of the six "supernatural talents," the faculty of comprehending in one instantaneous view, or by intuition, all beings in all worlds.]
10056{_}3472{_}[Footnote 4: This was Brahma, the first person of the Brahmanical Trimurti, adopted by Buddhism, but placed in an inferior position, and surpassed by every Buddhist saint who attains to bodhi.]
10056{_}3473{_}[Footnote 5: A note of Mr. Beal says on this:--"General Cunningham, who visited the spot (1862), found a pillar, evidently of the age of Asoka, with a well-carved elephant on the top, which, however, was minus trunk and tail.
10056{_}3474{_}He supposes this to be the pillar seen by Fa-hien, who mistook the top of it for a lion.
10056{_}3475{_}It is possible such a mistake may have been made, as in the account of one of the pillars at Sravasti, Fa-hien says an ox formed the capital, whilst Hsuean-chwang calls it an elephant."]
10056{_}3476{_}[Footnote 6: These three predecessors of Sakya-muni were the three Buddhas of the present or Maha-bhadra Kalpa, of which he was the fourth, and Maitreya is to be the fifth and last.
10056{_}3477{_}They were: (i) Kra-kuchanda, "he who readily solves all doubts"; a scion of the Kasyapa family.
10056{_}3478{_}Human life reached in his time forty thousand years, and so many persons were converted by him.
10056{_}3479{_}(2) Kanakamuni, "body radiant with the color of pure gold"; of the same family.
10056{_}3480{_}Human life reached in his time thirty thousand years, and so many persons were converted by him.
10056{_}3481{_}(3) Kasyapa, "swallower of light."
10056{_}3482{_}Human life reached in his time twenty thousand years, and so many persons were converted by him.]
10056{_}3483{_}[Footnote 7: This would seem to be absurd; but the writer evidently intended to convey the idea that there was something mysterious about the number of the topes.]
10056{_}3484{_}CHAPTER XVIII  ~Buddha's Subjects of Discourse~   Fa-Hien stayed at the Dragon vihara till after the summer retreat, [1] and then, travelling to the southeast for seven yojanas, he arrived at the city of Kanyakubja, lying along the Ganges.
10056{_}3485{_}There are two monasteries in it, the inmates of which are students of the hinayana.
10056{_}3486{_}At a distance from the city of six or seven li, on the west, on the northern bank of the Ganges, is a place where Buddha preached the Law to his disciples.
10056{_}3487{_}It has been handed down that his subjects of discourse were such as "The bitterness and vanity of life as impermanent and uncertain," and that "The body is as a bubble or foam on the water."
10056{_}3488{_}At this spot a tope was erected, and still exists.
10056{_}3489{_}Having crossed the Ganges, and gone south for three yojanas, the travellers arrived at a village named A-le, containing places where Buddha preached the Law, where he sat, and where he walked, at all of which topes have been built.
10056{_}3490{_}[Footnote 1: This was, probably, in A.D.
10056{_}3491{_}405.]
10056{_}3492{_}CHAPTER XIX  ~Legend of Buddha's Danta-kashtha~   Going on from this to the southeast for three yojanas, they came to the great kingdom of Sha-che.
10056{_}3493{_}As you go out of the city of Sha-che by the southern gate, on the east of the road is the place where Buddha, after he had chewed his willow branch, stuck it in the ground, when it forthwith grew up seven cubits, at which height it remained, neither increasing nor diminishing.
10056{_}3494{_}The Brahmans, with their contrary doctrines, became angry and jealous.
10056{_}3495{_}Sometimes they cut the tree down, sometimes they plucked it up, and cast it to a distance, but it grew again on the same spot as at first.
10056{_}3496{_}Here also is the place where the four Buddhas walked and sat, and at which a tope was built that is still existing.
10056{_}3497{_}CHAPTER XX  ~The Jetavana Vihara--Legends of Buddha~   Going on from this to the south, for eight yojanas, the travellers came to the city of Sravasti in the kingdom of Kosala, in which the inhabitants were few and far between, amounting in all only to a few more than two hundred families; the city where king Prasenajit ruled, and the place of the old vihara of Maha-prajapati; [1] of the well and walls of the house of the Vaisya head Sudatta; [2] and where the Angulimalya [3] became an Arhat, and his body was afterwards burned on his attaining to pari-nirvana.
10056{_}3498{_}At all these places topes were subsequently erected, which are still existing in the city.
10056{_}3499{_}The Brahmans, with their contrary doctrine, became full of hatred and envy in their hearts, and wished to destroy them, but there came from the heavens such a storm of crashing thunder and flashing lightning that they were not able in the end to effect their purpose.
10056{_}3500{_}As you go out from the city by the south gate, and one thousand two hundred paces from it, the Vais'ya head Sudatta built a vihara, facing the south; and when the door was open, on each side of it there was a stone pillar, with the figure of a wheel on the top of that on the left, and the figure of an ox on the top of that on the right.
10056{_}3501{_}On the left and right of the building the ponds of water clear and pure, the thickets of trees always luxuriant, and the numerous flowers of various hues, constituted a lovely scene, the whole forming what is called the Jetavana vihara.
10056{_}3502{_}When Buddha went up to the Trayastrimsas heaven, and preached the Law for the benefit of his mother, after he had been absent for ninety days, Prasenajit, longing to see him, caused an image of him to be carved in Gosirsha Chandana wood, and put in the place where he usually sat.
10056{_}3503{_}When Buddha, on his return entered the vihara, this image immediately left its place, and came forth to meet him.
10056{_}3504{_}Buddha said to it, "Return to your seat.
10056{_}3505{_}After I have attained to pari-nirvana, you will serve as a pattern to the four classes of my disciples," [4] and on this the image returned to its seat.
10056{_}3506{_}This was the very first of all the images of Buddha, and that which men subsequently copied.
10056{_}3507{_}Buddha then removed, and dwelt in a small vihara on the south side of the other, a different place from that containing the image, and twenty paces distant from it.
10056{_}3508{_}The Jetavana vihara was originally of seven stories.
10056{_}3509{_}The kings and people of the countries around vied with one another in their offerings, hanging up about it silken streamers and canopies, scattering flowers, burning incense, and lighting lamps, so as to make the night as bright as the day.
10056{_}3510{_}This they did day after day without ceasing.
10056{_}3511{_}It happened that a rat, carrying in its mouth the wick of a lamp, set one of the streamers or canopies on fire, which caught the vihara, and the seven stories were all consumed.
10056{_}3512{_}The kings, with their officers and people, were all very sad and distressed, supposing that the sandalwood image had been burned; but lo!
10056{_}3513{_}after four or five days, when the door of a small vihara on the east was opened, there was immediately seen the original image.
10056{_}3514{_}They were all greatly rejoiced, and cooperated in restoring the vihara.
10056{_}3515{_}When they had succeeded in completing two stories, they removed the image back to its former place.
10056{_}3516{_}When Fa-hien and Tao-ching first arrived at the Jetavana monastery, and thought how the World-honored one had formerly resided there for twenty-five years, painful reflections arose in their minds.
10056{_}3517{_}Born in a border-land, along with their like-minded friends, they had travelled through so many kingdoms; some of those friends had returned to their own land, and some had died, proving the impermanence and uncertainty of life; and today they saw the place where Buddha had lived now unoccupied by him.
10056{_}3518{_}They were melancholy through their pain of heart, and the crowd of monks came out, and asked them from what kingdom they were come.
10056{_}3519{_}"We are come," they replied, "from the land of Han."
10056{_}3520{_}"Strange," said the monks with a sigh, "that men of a border country should be able to come here in search of our Law!"
10056{_}3521{_}Then they said to one another, "During all the time that we, preceptors and monks, have succeeded to one another, we have never seen men of Han, followers of our system, arrive here."
10056{_}3522{_}Four li to the northwest of the vihara there is a grove called "The Getting of Eyes."
10056{_}3523{_}Formerly there were five hundred blind men, who lived here in order that they might be near the vihara.
10056{_}3524{_}Buddha preached his Law to them, and they all got their eyesight.
10056{_}3525{_}Full of joy, they stuck their staves in the earth, and with their heads and faces on the ground, did reverence.
10056{_}3526{_}The staves immediately began to grow, and they grew to be great.
10056{_}3527{_}People made much of them, and no one dared to cut them down, so that they came to form a grove.
10056{_}3528{_}It was in this way that it got its name, and most of the Jetavana monks, after they had taken their mid-day meal, went to the grove, and sat there in meditation.
10056{_}3529{_}Six or seven li northeast from the Jetavana, mother Vaisakha built another vihara, to which she invited Buddha and his monks, and which is still existing.
10056{_}3530{_}To each of the great residences for the monks at the Jetavana vihara there were two gates, one facing the east and the other facing the north.
10056{_}3531{_}The park containing the whole was the space of ground which the Vaisaya head, Sudatta, purchased by covering it with gold coins.
10056{_}3532{_}The vihara was exactly in the centre.
10056{_}3533{_}Here Buddha lived for a longer time than at any other place, preaching his Law and converting men.
10056{_}3534{_}At the places where he walked and sat they also subsequently reared topes, each having its particular name; and here was the place where Sundari [5] murdered a person and then falsely charged Buddha with the crime.
10056{_}3535{_}Outside the east gate of the Jetavana, at a distance of seventy paces to the north, on the west of the road, Buddha held a discussion with the advocates of the ninety-six schemes of erroneous doctrine, when the king and his great officers, the householders, and people were all assembled in crowds to hear it.
10056{_}3536{_}Then a woman belonging to one of the erroneous systems, by name Chanchamana, prompted by the envious hatred in her heart, and having put on extra clothes in front of her person, so as to give her the appearance of being with child, falsely accused Buddha before all the assembly of having acted unlawfully towards her.
10056{_}3537{_}On this, Sakra, Ruler of Devas, changed himself and some devas into white mice, which bit through the strings about her waist; and when this was done, the extra clothes which she wore dropped down on the ground.
10056{_}3538{_}The earth at the same time was rent, and she went down alive into hell.
10056{_}3539{_}This also is the place where Devadatta, trying with empoisoned claws to injure Buddha, went down alive into hell.
10056{_}3540{_}Men subsequently set up marks to distinguish where both these events took place.
10056{_}3541{_}Further, at the place where the discussion took place, they reared a vihara rather more than sixty cubits high, having in it an image of Buddha in a sitting posture.
10056{_}3542{_}On the east of the road there was a devalaya [6] of one of the contrary systems, called "The Shadow Covered," right opposite the vihara on the place of discussion, with only the road between them, and also rather more than sixty cubits high.
10056{_}3543{_}The reason why it was called "The Shadow Covered" was this: When the sun was in the west, the shadow of the vihara of the World-honored one fell on the devalaya of a contrary system; but when the sun was in the east, the shadow of that devalaya was diverted to the north, and never fell on the vihara of Buddha.
10056{_}3544{_}The malbelievers regularly employed men to watch their devalaya, to sweep and water all about it, to burn incense, light the lamps, and present offerings; but in the morning the lamps were found to have been suddenly removed, and in the vihara of Buddha.
10056{_}3545{_}The Brahmans were indignant, and said, "Those Sramanas take our lamps and use them for their own service of Buddha, but we will not stop our service for you!"
10056{_}3546{_}[7] On that night the Brahmans themselves kept watch, when they saw the deva spirits which they served take the lamps and go three times round the vihara of Buddha and present offerings.
10056{_}3547{_}After this administration to Buddha they suddenly disappeared.
10056{_}3548{_}The Brahmans thereupon knowing how great was the spiritual power of Buddha, forthwith left their families, and became monks.
10056{_}3549{_}It has been handed down, that, near the time when these things occurred, around the Jetavana vihara there were ninety-eight monasteries, in all of which there were monks residing, excepting only in one place which was vacant.
10056{_}3550{_}In this Middle Kingdom there are ninety-six sorts of views, erroneous and different from our system, all of which recognize this world and the future world and the connection between them.
10056{_}3551{_}Each has its multitude of followers, and they all beg their food: only they do not carry the alms-bowl.
10056{_}3552{_}They also, moreover, seek to acquire the blessing of good deeds on unfrequented ways, setting up on the roadside houses of charity, where rooms, couches, beds, and food and drink are supplied to travellers, and also to monks, coming and going as guests, the only difference being in the time for which those parties remain.
10056{_}3553{_}There are also companies of the followers of Devadatta still existing.
10056{_}3554{_}They regularly make offerings to the three previous Buddhas, but not to Sakyamuni Buddha.
10056{_}3555{_}Four li southeast from the city of Sravasti, a tope has been erected at the place where the World-honored one encountered king Virudhaha, when he wished to attack the kingdom of Shay-e, and took his stand before him at the side of the road.
10056{_}3556{_}[Footnote 1: Explained by "Path of Love," and "Lord of Life."
10056{_}3557{_}Prajapati was aunt and nurse of Sakyamuni, the first woman admitted to the monkhood, and the first superior of the first Buddhistic convent.
10056{_}3558{_}She is yet to become a Buddha.]
10056{_}3559{_}[Footnote 2: Sudatta, meaning "almsgiver," was the original name of Anatha-pindika, a wealthy householder, or Vaisya head, of Sravasti, famous for his liberality.
10056{_}3560{_}Of his old house, only the well and walls remained at the time of Fa-hien's visit to Sravasti.]
10056{_}3561{_}[Footnote 3: The Angulimalya were a sect or set of Sivaitic fanatics, who made assassination a religious act.
10056{_}3562{_}The one of them here mentioned had joined them by the force of circumstances.
10056{_}3563{_}Being converted by Buddha, he became a monk.]
10056{_}3564{_}[Footnote 4: Arya, meaning "honorable," "venerable," is a title given only to those who have mastered the four spiritual truths:--(i) that "misery" is a necessary condition of all sentient existence; this is duhka: (ii) that the "accumulation" of misery is caused by the passions; this is samudaya: (iii) that the "extinction" of passion is possible; this is nirodha: and (iv) that the "path" leads to the extinction of passion; which is marga.
10056{_}3565{_}According to their attainment of these truths, the Aryas, or followers of Buddha, are distinguished into four classes--Srotapannas, Sakridagamins, Anagamins, and Arhats.]
10056{_}3566{_}[Footnote 5: Hsuean-chwang does not give the name of this murderer; see in Julien's "Vie et Voyages de Hiouen-thsang "--"a heretical Brahman killed a woman and calumniated Buddha."
10056{_}3567{_}See also the fuller account in Beal's "Records of Western Countries," where the murder is committed by several Brahmacharins.
10056{_}3568{_}In this passage Beal makes Sundari to be the name of the murdered person.
10056{_}3569{_}But the text cannot be so construed.]
10056{_}3570{_}[Footnote 6: A devalaya is a place in which a deva is worshipped--a general name for all Brahmanical temples.]
10056{_}3571{_}[Footnote 7: Their speech was somewhat unconnected, but natural enough in the circumstances.
10056{_}3572{_}Compare the whole account with the narrative in 1 Samuel v. about the Ark and Dagon, that "twice-battered god of Palestine."]
10056{_}3573{_}CHAPTER XXI  ~The Three Predecessors of Sakyamuni~   Fifty li to the west of the city brings the traveller to a town named Too-wei, the birthplace of Kasyapa Buddha.
10056{_}3574{_}At the place where he and his father met, and at that where he attained to pari-nirvana, topes were erected.
10056{_}3575{_}Over the entire relic of the whole body of him, the Kasyapa Tathagata, a great tope was also erected.
10056{_}3576{_}Going on southeast from the city of Sravasti for twelve yojanas, the travellers came to a town named Na-pei-kea, the birthplace of Krakuchanda Buddha.
10056{_}3577{_}At the place where he and his father met, and at that where he attained to pari-nirvana, topes were erected.
10056{_}3578{_}Going north from here less than a yojana, they came to a town which had been the birthplace of Kanakamuni Buddha.
10056{_}3579{_}At the place where he and his father met, and where he attained to pari-nirvana, topes were erected.
10056{_}3580{_}CHAPTER XXII  ~Legends of Buddha's Birth~   Less than a yojana to the east from this brought them to the city of Kapilavastu; but in it there was neither king nor people.
10056{_}3581{_}All was mound and desolation.
10056{_}3582{_}Of inhabitants there were only some monks and a score or two of families of the common people.
10056{_}3583{_}At the spot where stood the old palace of king Suddhodana there have been made images of his eldest son and his mother; and at the places where that son appeared mounted on a white elephant when he entered his mother's womb, and where he turned his carriage round on seeing the sick man after he had gone out of the city by the eastern gate, topes have been erected.
10056{_}3584{_}The places were also pointed out where the rishi A-e inspected the marks of Buddhaship on the body of the heir-apparent when an infant; where, when he was in company with Nanda and others, on the elephant being struck down and drawn on one side, he tossed it away; [1] where he shot an arrow to the southeast, and it went a distance of thirty li, then entering the ground and making a spring to come forth, which men subsequently fashioned into a well from which travellers might drink; where, after he had attained to Wisdom, Buddha returned and saw the king, his father; where five hundred Sakyas quitted their families and did reverence to Upali [2] while the earth shook and moved in six different ways; where Buddha preached his Law to the devas, and the four deva kings and others kept the four doors of the hall, so that even the king, his father, could not enter; where Buddha sat under a nyagrodha tree, which is still standing, with his face to the east, and his aunt Maha-prajapati presented him with a Sanghali; and where king Vaidurya slew the seed of Sakya, and they all in dying became Srotapannas.
10056{_}3585{_}[3] A tope was erected at this last place, which is still existing.
10056{_}3586{_}Several li northeast from the city was the king's field, where the heir-apparent sat under a tree, and looked at the ploughers.
10056{_}3587{_}Fifty li east from the city was a garden, named Lumbini, where the queen entered the pond and bathed.
10056{_}3588{_}Having come forth from the pond on the northern bank, after walking twenty paces, she lifted up her hand, laid hold of a branch of a tree, and, with her face to the east, gave birth to the heir-apparent.
10056{_}3589{_}When he fell to the ground, he immediately walked seven paces.
10056{_}3590{_}Two dragon-kings appeared and washed his body.
10056{_}3591{_}At the place where they did so, there was immediately formed a well, and from it, as well as from the above pond, where the queen bathed, the monks even now constantly take the water, and drink it.
10056{_}3592{_}There are four places of regular and fixed occurrence in the history of all Buddhas: first, the place where they attained to perfect Wisdom and became Buddha; second, the place where they turned the wheel of the Law; third, the place where they preached the Law, discoursed of righteousness, and discomfited the advocates of erroneous doctrines; and fourth, the place where they came down, after going up to the Trayastrimsas heaven to preach the Law for the benefit of their mothers.
10056{_}3593{_}Other places in connection with them became remarkable, according to the manifestations which were made at them at particular times.
10056{_}3594{_}The country of Kapilavastu is a great scene of empty desolation.
10056{_}3595{_}The inhabitants are few and far between.
10056{_}3596{_}On the roads people have to be on their guard against white elephants [4] and lions, and should not travel incautiously.
10056{_}3597{_}[Footnote 1: The Lichchhavis of Vaisali had sent to the young prince a very fine elephant; but when it was near Kapilavastu, Deva-datta, out of envy, killed it with a blow of his fist.
10056{_}3598{_}Nanda (not Ananda, but a half-brother of Siddhartha), coming that way, saw the carcass lying on the road, and pulled it on one side; but the Bodhisattva, seeing it there, took it by the tail, and tossed it over seven fences and ditches, when the force of its fall made a great ditch.]
10056{_}3599{_}[Footnote 2: They did this, probably, to show their humility, for Upali was only a Sudra by birth, and had been a barber; so from the first did Buddhism assert its superiority to the conditions of rank and caste.
10056{_}3600{_}Upali was distinguished by his knowledge of the rules of discipline, and praised on that account by Buddha.
10056{_}3601{_}He was one of the three leaders of the first synod, and the principal compiler of the original Vinaya books.]
10056{_}3602{_}[Footnote 3: The Srotapannas are the first class of saints, who are not to be reborn in a lower sphere, but attain to nirvana after having been reborn seven times consecutively as men or devas.
10056{_}3603{_}The Chinese editions state there were one thousand of the Sakya seed.
10056{_}3604{_}The general account is that they were five hundred, all maidens, who refused to take their place in king Vaidurya's harem, and were in consequence taken to a pond, and had their hands and feet cut off.
10056{_}3605{_}There Buddha came to them, had their wounds dressed, and preached to them the Law.
10056{_}3606{_}They died in the faith, and were reborn in the region of the four Great Kings.
10056{_}3607{_}Thence they came back and visited Buddha at Jetavana in the night, and there they obtained the reward of Srotapanna.]
10056{_}3608{_}[Footnote 4: Fa-hien does not say that he himself saw any of these white elephants, nor does he speak of the lions as of any particular color.
10056{_}3609{_}We shall find by and by, in a note further on, that, to make them appear more terrible, they are spoken of as "black."]
10056{_}3610{_}CHAPTER XXIII  ~Legends of Rama and its Tope~   East from Buddha's birthplace, and at a distance of five yojanas, there is a kingdom called Rama.
10056{_}3611{_}The king of this country, having obtained one portion of the relics of Buddha's body, returned with it and built over it a tope, named the Rama tope.
10056{_}3612{_}By the side of it there was a pool, and in the pool a dragon, which constantly kept watch over the tope, and presented offerings at it day and night.
10056{_}3613{_}When king Asoka came forth into the world, he wished to destroy the eight topes over the relics, and to build instead of them eighty-four thousand topes.
10056{_}3614{_}[1] After he had thrown down the seven others, he wished next to destroy this tope.
10056{_}3615{_}But then the dragon showed itself, and took the king into its palace; when he had seen all the things provided for offerings, it said to him, "If you are able with your offerings to exceed these, you can destroy the tope, and take it all away.
10056{_}3616{_}I will not contend with you."
10056{_}3617{_}The king, however, knew that such appliances for offerings were not to be had anywhere in the world, and thereupon returned without carrying out his purpose.
10056{_}3618{_}Afterwards, the ground all about became overgrown with vegetation, and there was nobody to sprinkle and sweep about the tope; but a herd of elephants came regularly, which brought water with their trunks to water the ground, and various kinds of flowers and incense, which they presented at the tope.
10056{_}3619{_}Once there came from one of the kingdoms a devotee to worship at the tope.
10056{_}3620{_}When he encountered the elephants he was greatly alarmed, and screened himself among the trees; but when he saw them go through with the offerings in the most proper manner, the thought filled him with great sadness--that there should be no monastery here, the inmates of which might serve the tope, but the elephants have to do the watering and sweeping.
10056{_}3621{_}Forthwith he gave up the great prohibitions by which he was bound, and resumed the status of a Sramanera.
10056{_}3622{_}With his own hands he cleared away the grass and trees, put the place in good order, and made it pure and clean.
10056{_}3623{_}By the power of his exhortations, he prevailed on the king of the country to form a residence for monks; and when that was done, he became head of the monastery.
10056{_}3624{_}At the present day there are monks residing in it.
10056{_}3625{_}This event is of recent occurrence; but in all the succession from that time till now, there has always been a Sramanera head of the establishment.
10056{_}3626{_}[Footnote 1: The bones of the human body are supposed to consist of 84,000 atoms, and hence the legend of Asoka's wish to build 84,000 topes, one over each atom of Sakyamuni's skeleton.]
10056{_}3627{_}CHAPTER XXIV  ~Where Buddha Renounced the World~   East from here four yojanas, there is the place where the heir-apparent sent back Chandaka, with his white horse; and there also a tope was erected.
10056{_}3628{_}Four yojanas to the east from this, the travellers came to the Charcoal tope, where there is also a monastery.
10056{_}3629{_}Going on twelve yojanas, still to the east, they came to the city of Kusanagara, on the north of which, between two trees, on the bank of the Nairanjana river, is the place where the World-honored one, with his head to the north, attained to pan-nirvana and died.
10056{_}3630{_}There also are the places where Subhadra, [1] the last of his converts, attained to Wisdom and became an Arhat; where in his coffin of gold they made offerings to the World-honored one for seven days, where the Vajrapani laid aside his golden club, and where the eight kings divided the relics of the burnt body: at all these places were built topes and monasteries, all of which are now existing.
10056{_}3631{_}In the city the inhabitants are few and far between, comprising only the families belonging to the different societies of monks.
10056{_}3632{_}Going from this to the southeast for twelve yojanas, they came to the place where the Lichchhavis wished to follow Buddha to the place of his pari-nirvana, and where, when he would not listen to them and they kept cleaving to him, unwilling to go away, he made to appear a large and deep ditch which they could not cross over, and gave them his alms-bowl, as a pledge of his regard, thus sending them back to their families.
10056{_}3633{_}There a stone pillar was erected with an account of this event engraved upon it.
10056{_}3634{_}[Footnote 1: A Brahman of Benares, said to have been one hundred and twenty years old, who came to learn from Buddha the very night he died.
10056{_}3635{_}Ananda would have repulsed him; but Buddha ordered him to be introduced; and then putting aside the ingenious but unimportant question which he propounded, preached to him the Law.
10056{_}3636{_}The Brahman was converted and attained at once to Arhatship.]
10056{_}3637{_}CHAPTER XXV  ~The Kingdom of Vaisali~   East from this city ten yojanas, the travellers came to the kingdom of Vaisali.
10056{_}3638{_}North of the city so named is a large forest, having in it the double-galleried vihara where Buddha dwelt, and the tope over half the body of Ananda.
10056{_}3639{_}Inside the city the woman Ambapali [1] built a vihara in honor of Buddha, which is now standing as it was at first.
10056{_}3640{_}Three li south of the city, on the west of the road, is the garden which the same Ambapali presented to Buddha, in which he might reside.
10056{_}3641{_}When Buddha was about to attain to his pari-nirvana, as he was quitting the city by the west gate, he turned round, and, beholding the city on his right, said to them, "Here I have taken my last walk."
10056{_}3642{_}Men subsequently built a tope at this spot.
10056{_}3643{_}Three li northwest of the city there is a tope called, "Bows and weapons laid down."
10056{_}3644{_}The reason why it got that name was this: The inferior wife of a king, whose country lay along the river Ganges, brought forth from her womb a ball of flesh.
