10056{_}4139{_}Some passages have been embodied in our version: but the translator did not give all, for the same reasons that prompted Pere Premare to give none--"they are full of allusions to things unfamiliar to us, and figures of speech very difficult for us to observe."
10056{_}4140{_}They are frequently, moreover, mere repetitions or amplifications of the prose parts; and being intended more for the ear than the eye, are rather adapted to the stage than to the closet.
10056{_}4141{_}His judgment may perhaps be swayed by partiality towards the subject of his own labors; but the translator cannot help thinking the plot and incidents of "The Sorrows of Han" superior to those of the "Orphan of Chaou"--though the genius of Voltaire contrived to make the last the ground-work of an excellent French tragedy.
10056{_}4142{_}Far is he, however, from entertaining the presumptuous expectation that a destiny of equal splendor awaits the present drama; and he will be quite satisfied if the reader has patience to read it to the end, and then pronounces it to be a somewhat curious sample of a very foreign literature.
10056{_}4143{_}JOHN FRANCIS DAVIS.
10056{_}4144{_}DRAMATIS PERSONAE  YUENTE, Emperor of China of the Dynasty Han.
10056{_}4145{_}HANCHENYU, K'han of the Tartars.
10056{_}4146{_}MAOUYENSHOW, a worthless Minister of the Emperor.
10056{_}4147{_}SHANGSHOO (a title), President of the Imperial Council.
10056{_}4148{_}CHANGSHEE (a title), Officer in waiting.
10056{_}4149{_}FANSHE (a title), Envoy of the K'han.
10056{_}4150{_}CHAOUKEUN, Lady, raised to be Princess of Han.
10056{_}4151{_}Tartar Soldiers, Female Attendants, Eunuchs.
10056{_}4152{_}The Scene is laid in the Tartar Camp on the Frontiers; and in the Palace of Han.
10056{_}4153{_}~THE SORROWS OF HAN~ [1]    ~PROLOGUE~   _Enter Hanchenyu, K'han [2] of the Tartars, reciting four verses_.
10056{_}4154{_}K'HAN.
10056{_}4155{_}The autumnal gale blows wildly through the grass,       amidst our woolen tents.
10056{_}4156{_}And the moon of night, shining on the rude huts, hears the       lament of the mournful pipe:   The countless hosts, with their bended horns, obey me as       their leader.
10056{_}4157{_}Our tribes are ten distinguished friends of the family of Han.
10056{_}4158{_}I am     Hanchenyu, the old inhabitant of the sandy waste; the sole ruler of     the northern regions.
10056{_}4159{_}The wild chase is our trade; battle and     conquest our chief occupation.
10056{_}4160{_}The Emperor Wunwong retired before     our Eastern tribes; Weikeang trembled at us, and sued for our     friendship.
10056{_}4161{_}The ancient title of our chiefs has in the course of     time been changed to that which I now bear.
10056{_}4162{_}When the two races of     Tsin and Han contended in battle, and filled the empire with tumult,     our tribes were in full power: numberless was the host of armed     warriors with their bended horns.
10056{_}4163{_}For seven days my ancestor hemmed     in with his forces the Emperor Kaoute; until, by the contrivance of     the minister, a treaty was concluded, and the Princesses of China     were yielded in marriage to our K'hans.
10056{_}4164{_}Since the time of Hoeyte and     the Empress Leuhow, [3] each successive generation has adhered to     the established rule, and sought our alliance with its daughters.
10056{_}4165{_}In     the reign of the late Emperor Seuente, my brothers contended with     myself for the rule of our nation, and its power was weakened until     the tribes elected me as their chief.
10056{_}4166{_}I am a real descendant of the     empire of Han.
10056{_}4167{_}I command a hundred thousand armed warriors.
10056{_}4168{_}We have     moved to the South, and approached the border, claiming an alliance     with the Imperial race.
10056{_}4169{_}Yesterday I despatched an envoy with     tributary presents to demand a princess in marriage; but know not if     the Emperor will ratify the engagement with the customary oaths.
10056{_}4170{_}The     fineness of the season has drawn away our chiefs on a hunting     excursion amidst the sandy steppes.
10056{_}4171{_}May they meet with success, for     we Tartars have no fields--our bows and arrows are our sole means of     subsistence.
10056{_}4172{_}_Enter Minister of Han, reciting verses_.
10056{_}4173{_}MINISTER.
10056{_}4174{_}Let a man have the heart of a kite, and the talons       of an eagle.
10056{_}4175{_}Let him deceive his superiors, and oppress those below       him;   Let him enlist flattery, insinuation, profligacy, and avarice       on his side,      And he will find them a lasting assistance through life.
10056{_}4176{_}I am no     other than Maouyenshow, a minister of the sovereign of Han.
10056{_}4177{_}By a     hundred arts of specious flattery and address I have deceived the     Emperor, until he places his whole delight in me alone.
10056{_}4178{_}My words he     listens to; and he follows my counsel.
10056{_}4179{_}Within the precincts of the     palace, as without them, who is there but bows before me--who is     there but trembles at my approach?
10056{_}4180{_}But observe the chief art which I     have learned: It is this: to persuade the Emperor to keep aloof from     his wise counsellors, and seek all his pleasures amidst the women of     his palace.
10056{_}4181{_}Thus it is that I strengthen my power and greatness.
10056{_}4182{_}But, in the midst of my lucubrations--Here comes the Emperor.
10056{_}4183{_}_Enter Emperor Yuente, attended by Eunuchs and Women_.
10056{_}4184{_}EMPEROR [_recites verses]_.
10056{_}4185{_}During the ten generations that     have succeeded our acquisition of Empire, my race has alone     possessed the four hundred districts of the world.
10056{_}4186{_}Long have the     frontiers been bound in tranquillity by the ties of mutual oaths.
10056{_}4187{_}And our pillow has been undisturbed by grief or anxiety.
10056{_}4188{_}Behold in     us the Emperor Yuente, of the race of Han.
10056{_}4189{_}Our ancestor Kaoute     emerged from a private station, and raised his family by     extinguishing the dynasty of Tsin, and slaughtering their race.
10056{_}4190{_}Ten     generations have passed away since he left this inheritance to us.
10056{_}4191{_}The four boundaries of the empire have been tranquil; the eight     regions at rest!
10056{_}4192{_}But not through our personal merits; we have wholly     depended on the exertions of our civil and military rulers.
10056{_}4193{_}On the     demise of our late father, the female inmates of the palace were all     dispersed, and our harem is now solitary and untenanted; but how     shall this be endured!
10056{_}4194{_}MINISTER.
10056{_}4195{_}Consider, sir, that even the thriving husbandman     may desire to change his partner; then why not your Majesty, whose     title is the Law of Heaven, whose possessions are the whole world!
10056{_}4196{_}May I advise that commissioners be despatched to search throughout     the empire for all of whatever rank that is most beautiful between     the ages of fifteen and twenty, for the peopling of the inner     palace.
10056{_}4197{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4198{_}You say well.
10056{_}4199{_}We appoint you at once our minister of     selection, and will invest you with a written authority.
10056{_}4200{_}Search     diligently through our realms; and when you have selected the most     worthy, let us be provided with portraits of each, as a means of     fixing our choice.
10056{_}4201{_}By the merits of your services, you may supply us     with an occasion of rewarding you on your return.
10056{_}4202{_}[_Exeunt_.
10056{_}4203{_}[Footnote 1: Han Koong Tsew, literally "Autumn in the Palace of Han"; but in Chinese, Autumn is emblematic of Sorrow, as Spring is of Joy, and may therefore be rendered by what it represents.]
10056{_}4204{_}[Footnote 2: In Chinese, Ko-ban.]
10056{_}4205{_}[Footnote 3: The mother of Hoeyte, a bold and able woman, who ruled for her son, the second emperor of Han.]
10056{_}4206{_}~ACT FIRST~    MINISTER [_repeats verses_].
10056{_}4207{_}The huge ingots of yellow gold I       appropriate to myself.
10056{_}4208{_}I heed not the seas of blood which flow by perverting the       laws.
10056{_}4209{_}During life I am determined to have abundance of riches; what care I     for the curses of mankind after my death?
10056{_}4210{_}Having received the     Emperor's commission to search far and wide for the most beautiful     damsels, I have fixed upon ninety and nine.
10056{_}4211{_}Their families were glad     to invite my selection by rich gifts, and the treasure that I have     amassed is not small.
10056{_}4212{_}On arriving yesterday at a district pertaining     to Chingtoo city, I met with a maiden, daughter of one Wongchang.
10056{_}4213{_}The brightness of her charms was piercing as an arrow.
10056{_}4214{_}She was     perfectly beautiful--and doubtless unparalleled in the whole empire.
10056{_}4215{_}But, unfortunately, her father is a cultivator of the land, not     possessed of much wealth.
10056{_}4216{_}When I insisted on a hundred ounces of     gold to secure her being the chief object of the imperial choice,     they first pleaded their poverty--and then, relying on her     extraordinary beauty, rejected my offers altogether.
10056{_}4217{_}I therefore     left them.
10056{_}4218{_}[_Considers awhile_.]
10056{_}4219{_}But no!----I have a better plan.
10056{_}4220{_}[_He knits his brows and matures his scheme_.]
10056{_}4221{_}I will disfigure her     portrait in such a manner that when it reaches the Emperor it shall     secure her being doomed to neglected seclusion.
10056{_}4222{_}Thus I shall     contrive to make her unhappy for life--Base is the man who delights     not in revenge!
10056{_}4223{_}[_Exit._   _Night_.--_Enter the Lady Chaoukeun, with two female attendants_.
10056{_}4224{_}CHAOUKEUN [_recites verses_].
10056{_}4225{_}Though raised to be an inhabitant       of the imperial dwelling     I have long been here without the good fortune to see       my prince.
10056{_}4226{_}This beautiful night must I pass in lonely solitude, with no     companion but my lute to solace my retirement.
10056{_}4227{_}I am a native of     Chingtoo city; and my father's occupation is husbandry.
10056{_}4228{_}My mother     dreamed on the day I was born that the light of the moon shone on     her bosom, but was soon cast low to the earth.
10056{_}4229{_}[1] I was just     eighteen years of age when chosen as an inhabitant of the imperial     palace; but the minister Maouyenshow, disappointed in the treasure     which he demanded on my account, disfigured my portrait in such a     manner as to keep me out of the Emperor's presence; and now I live     in neglected solitude.
10056{_}4230{_}While at home, I learned a little music, and     could play a few airs on the lute.
10056{_}4231{_}Thus sorrowing in the stillness     of midnight, let me practise one of my songs to dispel my griefs.
10056{_}4232{_}[_Begins to play on the lute_.
10056{_}4233{_}_Enter Emperor, attended by a Eunuch, carrying a light_.
10056{_}4234{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4235{_}Since the beauties were selected to grace our palace,     we have not yet discovered a worthy object on whom to fix our     preference.
10056{_}4236{_}Vexed and disappointed, we pass this day of leisure     roaming in search of her who may be destined for our imperial     choice.
10056{_}4237{_}[_Hears the lute._] Is not that some lady's lute?
10056{_}4238{_}ATTENDANT.
10056{_}4239{_}It is.--I hasten to advise her of your Majesty's     approach.
10056{_}4240{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4241{_}No, hold!
10056{_}4242{_}Keeper of the yellow gate, discover to     what part of our palace that lady pertains; and bid her approach our     presence; but beware lest you alarm her.
10056{_}4243{_}ATTENDANT [_approaches in the direction of the sound, and     speaks_].
10056{_}4244{_}What lady plays there?
10056{_}4245{_}The Emperor comes!
10056{_}4246{_}approach to meet     him.
10056{_}4247{_}[_Lady advances_.
10056{_}4248{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4249{_}Keeper of the yellow gate, see that the light burns     brightly within your gauze [2] lamp, and hold it nearer to us.
10056{_}4250{_}LADY _[approaching_].
10056{_}4251{_}Had your handmaid but known it was     your Majesty, she would have been less tardy; forgive, then, this     delay.
10056{_}4252{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4253{_}Truly this is a very perfect beauty!
10056{_}4254{_}From what     quarter come such superior charms?
10056{_}4255{_}LADY.
10056{_}4256{_}My name is Chaoukeun: my father cultivates at Chingtoo     the fields which he has derived from his family.
10056{_}4257{_}Born in an humble     station, I am ignorant of the manners that befit a palace.
10056{_}4258{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4259{_}But with such uncommon attractions, what chance     has kept you from our sight?
10056{_}4260{_}LADY.
10056{_}4261{_}When I was chosen by the minister Maouyenshow, he     demanded of my father an amount of treasure which our poverty could     not supply; he therefore disfigured my portrait, by representing a     scar under the eyes, and caused me to be consigned to seclusion and     neglect.
10056{_}4262{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4263{_}Keeper of the yellow gate, bring us that picture,     that we may view it.
10056{_}4264{_}[_Sees the picture_.]
10056{_}4265{_}Ah, how has he dimmed the     purity of the gem, bright as the waves in autumn.
10056{_}4266{_}[_To the     attendant_] Transmit our pleasure to the officer of the guard, to     behead Maouyenshow and report to us his execution.
10056{_}4267{_}LADY.
10056{_}4268{_}My parents, sir, are subject to the tax [3] in our native     district.
10056{_}4269{_}Let me entreat your Majesty to remit their contributions     and extend favor towards them!
10056{_}4270{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4271{_}That shall readily be done.
10056{_}4272{_}Approach and hear our     imperial pleasure.
10056{_}4273{_}We create you a Princess of our palace.
10056{_}4274{_}LADY.
10056{_}4275{_}How unworthy is your handmaid of such gracious distinction!
10056{_}4276{_}[_Goes through the form of returning thanks_.]
10056{_}4277{_}Early to-morrow I     attend your Majesty's commands in this place.
10056{_}4278{_}The Emperor is gone:     let the attendants close the doors:--I will retire to rest.
10056{_}4279{_}_[Exit._    [Footnote 1: Boding a short but fatal distinction to her offspring.]
10056{_}4280{_}[Footnote 2: Instead of glass, to defend it from the wind.]
10056{_}4281{_}[Footnote 3: The principal taxes in China are the land-tax, customs, salt monopoly, and personal service; which last is the source of much oppression to the lowest orders, who have nothing but their labor to contribute.]
10056{_}4282{_}~ACT SECOND~    _Enter K'han of the Tartars, at the head of his Tribes_.
10056{_}4283{_}K'HAN.
10056{_}4284{_}I lately sent an envoy to the sovereign of Han, with     the demand of a princess in marriage; but the Emperor has returned a     refusal, under the plea that the princess is yet too young.
10056{_}4285{_}This     answer gives me great trouble.
10056{_}4286{_}Had he not plenty of ladies in his     palace, of whom he might have sent me one?
10056{_}4287{_}The difference was of     little consequence.
10056{_}4288{_}[1] Let me recall my envoy with all speed, for I     must invade the South with out forces.
10056{_}4289{_}And yet I am unwilling to     break a truce of so many years' standing!
10056{_}4290{_}We must see how matters     turn out, and be guided by the event.
10056{_}4291{_}_Enter Minister of Han_.
10056{_}4292{_}MINISTER.
10056{_}4293{_}The severity with which I extorted money, in the     selection of beauties for the palace, led me to disfigure the     picture of Chaoukeun, and consign her to neglected seclusion.
10056{_}4294{_}But     the Emperor fell in with her, obtained the truth, and condemned me     to lose my head.
10056{_}4295{_}I contrived to make my escape--though I have no     home to receive me.
10056{_}4296{_}I will take this true portrait of Chaoukeun and     show it to the Tartar K'han, persuading him to demand her from the     Emperor, who will no doubt be obliged to yield her up.
10056{_}4297{_}A long     journey has brought me to this spot, and from the troops of men and     horses I conclude I have reached the Tartar camp.
10056{_}4298{_}[_Addresses     himself to somebody_] Leader, inform King Hanchenyu that a great     minister of the empire of Han is come to wait on him.
10056{_}4299{_}K'HAN [_on being informed_].
10056{_}4300{_}Command him to approach.
10056{_}4301{_}[_Seeing Maouyenshow_] What person are you?
10056{_}4302{_}MINISTER.
10056{_}4303{_}I am a minister of Han.
10056{_}4304{_}In the western palace of     the Emperor is a lady, named Chaoukeun, of rare and surpassing     charms.
10056{_}4305{_}When your envoy, great king, came to demand a princess, this     lady would have answered the summons, but the Emperor of Han could     not bring himself to part with her, and refused to yield her up.
10056{_}4306{_}I     repeatedly renewed my bitter reproaches, and asked how he could     bear, for the sake of a woman's beauty, to implicate the welfare of     two nations.
10056{_}4307{_}For this the Emperor would have beheaded me; and I     therefore escaped with the portrait of the lady, which I present,     great king, to yourself.
10056{_}4308{_}Should you send away an envoy with the     picture to demand her, she must certainly be delivered up.
10056{_}4309{_}Here is     the portrait.
10056{_}4310{_}[_Hands it up_.
10056{_}4311{_}K'HAN.
10056{_}4312{_}Whence could so beautiful a female have appeared     in the world!
10056{_}4313{_}If I can only obtain her, my wishes are complete.
10056{_}4314{_}Immediately shall an envoy be despatched, and my ministers prepare a     letter to the Emperor of Han, demanding her in marriage as the     condition of peace.
10056{_}4315{_}Should he refuse, I will presently invade the     South: his hills and rivers shall be exposed to ravage.
10056{_}4316{_}Our warriors     will commence by hunting, as they proceed on their way; and thus     gradually entering the frontiers, I shall be ready to act as may     best suit the occasion.
10056{_}4317{_}[_Exit._  _The Palace of Han.
10056{_}4318{_}Enter Lady, attended by females_.
10056{_}4319{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4320{_}A long period has elapsed since I had to thank his     Majesty for his choice.
10056{_}4321{_}The Emperor's fondness for me is so great,     that he has still neglected to hold a court.
10056{_}4322{_}I hear he is now gone     to the hall of audience, and will therefore ornament myself at my     toilet and be ready to wait on him at his return.
10056{_}4323{_}[_Stands opposite     a mirror_.
10056{_}4324{_}_Enter Emperor_.
10056{_}4325{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4326{_}Since we first met with Chaoukeun in the western     palace, we have been as it were deranged and intoxicated; a long     interval has elapsed since we held a court; and on entering the hall     of audience this day, we waited not until the assembly had     dispersed, but returned hither to obtain a sight of her.
10056{_}4327{_}[_Perceiving the Princess_.]
10056{_}4328{_}Let us not alarm her, but observe in     secret what she is doing.
10056{_}4329{_}[_Comes close behind and looks over her._] Reflected in that round     mirror, she resembles the Lady in the Moon.
10056{_}4330{_}[2]  _Enter President, and an Officer in waiting_.
10056{_}4331{_}PRESIDENT [_recites verses._] Ministers should devote themselves           to the regulation of the empire; They should be occupied with public     cares in the hall of government.
10056{_}4332{_}But they do nought but attend at          the banquets in the palace.
10056{_}4333{_}When have they employed a single day in     the service of their prince?
10056{_}4334{_}This day, when the audience was concluded, an envoy arrived from the     Tartars to demand Chaoukeun in marriage, as the only condition of     peace.
10056{_}4335{_}It is my duty to report this to his Majesty, who has retired     to his western palace.
10056{_}4336{_}Here I must enter.
10056{_}4337{_}[_Perceiving the     Emperor._] I report to your Majesty that Hanchenyu, the leader of     the northern foreigners, sends an envoy to declare that Maouyenshow     has presented to him the portrait of the princess, and that he     demands her in marriage as the only condition of peace.
10056{_}4338{_}If refused,     he will invade the South with a great power, and our rivers and     hills will be exposed to rapine.
10056{_}4339{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4340{_}In vain do we maintain and send forth armies; vain     are the crowds of civil and military officers about our palace!
10056{_}4341{_}Which of them will drive back for us these foreign troops?
10056{_}4342{_}They are     all afraid of the Tartar swords and arrows!
10056{_}4343{_}But if they cannot exert     themselves to expel the barbarians, why call for the princess to     propitiate them?
10056{_}4344{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4345{_}The foreigners say that through your Majesty's     devoted fondness for the princess, the affairs of your empire are     falling into ruin.
10056{_}4346{_}They declare that if the government does not     yield her up, they will put their army in motion, and subdue the     country.
10056{_}4347{_}Your servant reflects, that Chow-wong [3] who lost his     empire and life entirely through his blind devotion to Takee, is a     fit example to warn your Majesty.
10056{_}4348{_}Our army is weak, and needs the     talents of a fit general.
10056{_}4349{_}Should we oppose the Tartars, and be     defeated, what will remain to us?
10056{_}4350{_}Let your Majesty give up your     fondness for the princess, to save your people.
10056{_}4351{_}OFFICER.
10056{_}4352{_}The envoy waits without for an audience.
10056{_}4353{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4354{_}Well; command that he approach us.
10056{_}4355{_}_Enter Envoy_.
10056{_}4356{_}ENVOY.
10056{_}4357{_}Hanchenyu, K'han of the Tartars, sends me, his minister,     to state before the great Sovereign of Han, that the Northern tribes     and the Southern empire have long been bound in peace by mutual     alliances; but that envoys being twice sent to demand a princess,     his requisitions have been refused.
10056{_}4358{_}The late minister, Maouyenshow,     took with him the portrait of a beautiful lady, and presented it to     the K'ban, who now sends me, his envoy, on purpose to demand the     Lady Chaoukeun, and no other, as the only condition of peace between     the two nations.
10056{_}4359{_}Should your Majesty refuse, the K'han has a     countless army of brave warriors, and will forthwith invade the     South to try the chances of war.
10056{_}4360{_}I trust your Majesty will not err     in your decision.
10056{_}4361{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4362{_}The envoy may retire to repose himself in his lodging.
10056{_}4363{_}[_Exit the Envoy_.]
10056{_}4364{_}Let our civil and military officers consult, and     report to us the best mode of causing the foreign troops to retire,     without yielding up the princess to propitiate them.
10056{_}4365{_}They take     advantage of the compliant softness of her temper.
10056{_}4366{_}Were the Empress     Leuhow alive--let her utter a word--which of them would dare to be     of a different opinion?
10056{_}4367{_}It would seem that, for the future, instead     of men for ministers, we need only have fair women to keep our     empire in peace.
10056{_}4368{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4369{_}In return for your Majesty's bounties, it is your     handmaid's duty to brave death to serve you.
10056{_}4370{_}I can cheerfully enter     into this foreign alliance, for the sake of producing peace, and     shall leave behind me a name still green in history.--But my     affection for your Majesty, how am I to lay aside!
10056{_}4371{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4372{_}Alas, I [4] know too well that I can do no more than     yourself!
10056{_}4373{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4374{_}I entreat your Majesty to sacrifice your love, and     think of the security of your Dynasty.
10056{_}4375{_}Hasten, sir, to send the     princess on her way!
10056{_}4376{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4377{_}Let her this day advance a stage on her journey,     and be presented to the envoy.--To-morrow we will repair as far as     the bridge of Pahling, and give her a parting feast.
10056{_}4378{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4379{_}Alas!
10056{_}4380{_}Sir, this may not be!
10056{_}4381{_}It will draw on us     the contempt of these barbarians.
10056{_}4382{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4383{_}We have complied with all our minister's propositions--shall     they not, then, accede to ours?
10056{_}4384{_}Be it as it may, we will witness her     departure--and then return home to hate the traitor Maouyenshow!
10056{_}4385{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4386{_}Unwillingly we advise that the princess be sacrificed     for the sake of peace; but the envoy is instructed to insist upon     her alone--and from ancient times, how often hath a nation suffered     for a woman's beauty!
10056{_}4387{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4388{_}Though I go into exile for the nation's good, yet ill     can I bear to part from your Majesty!
10056{_}4389{_}_[Exeunt._   [Footnote 1: The honor of the imperial alliance being the chief object.]
10056{_}4390{_}[Footnote 2: Changngo, the goddess of the moon, gives her name to the finely curved eyebrows of the Chinese ladies, which are compared to the lunar crescent when only a day or two old.]
10056{_}4391{_}[Footnote 3: Chow-wong was the last of the Shang dynasty, and infamous by his debaucheries and cruelties, in concert with his empress Takee, the Theodora of Chinese history.]
10056{_}4392{_}[Footnote 4: The imperial pronoun "Tchin," _me_, is with very good taste supplied by _I_ in these impassioned passages.]
10056{_}4393{_}~ACT THIRD~    _Enter Envoy, escorting the Princess, with a band of music_.
10056{_}4394{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4395{_}Thus was I, in spite of the treachery of Maouyenshow,     who disfigured my portrait, seen and exalted by his Majesty; but the     traitor presented a truer likeness to the Tartar king, who comes at     the head of an army to demand me, with a threat of seizing the     country.
10056{_}4396{_}There is no remedy--I must be yielded up to propitiate the     invaders!
10056{_}4397{_}How shall I bear the rigors--the winds and frosts of that     foreign land!
10056{_}4398{_}It has been said of old, that "surpassing beauty is     often coupled with an unhappy fate."
10056{_}4399{_}Let me grieve, then, without     entertaining fruitless resentment at the effects of my own     attractions.
10056{_}4400{_}_Enter Emperor, attended by his several officers_.
10056{_}4401{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4402{_}This day we take leave of the princess at Pahling     bridge!
10056{_}4403{_}[_To his ministers_.]
10056{_}4404{_}Can ye not devise a way to send out     these foreign troops, without yielding up the princess for the sake     of peace?
10056{_}4405{_}[_Descends from his horse and seems to grieve with     Chaoukeun_.]
10056{_}4406{_}Let our attendants delay awhile, till we have conferred     the parting cup.
10056{_}4407{_}ENVOY.
10056{_}4408{_}Lady, let us urge you to proceed on your way--the     sky darkens, and night is coming on.
10056{_}4409{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4410{_}Alas!
10056{_}4411{_}when shall I again behold your Majesty?
10056{_}4412{_}I     will take off my robes of distinction and leave them behind me.
10056{_}4413{_}To-day in the palace of Han--to-morrow I shall be espoused to a     stranger.
10056{_}4414{_}I cease to wear these splendid vestments--they shall no     longer adorn my beauty in the eyes of men.
10056{_}4415{_}ENVOY.
10056{_}4416{_}Again let us urge you, princess, to depart; we have     delayed but too long already!
10056{_}4417{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4418{_}'Tis done!--Princess, when you are gone, let your     thoughts forbear to dwell with sorrow and resentment upon us!
10056{_}4419{_}[_They     part_.]
10056{_}4420{_}And am I the great Monarch of the line of Han?
10056{_}4421{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4422{_}Let your Majesty cease to dwell with such grief     upon this subject!
10056{_}4423{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4424{_}She is gone!
10056{_}4425{_}In vain have we maintained those     armed heroes on the frontier.
10056{_}4426{_}[1] Mention but swords and spears, and     they tremble at their hearts like a young deer.
10056{_}4427{_}The princess has     this day performed what belonged to themselves: and yet they affect     the semblance of men!
10056{_}4428{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4429{_}Your Majesty is entreated to return to the palace:     dwell not so bitterly, Sir, on her memory:--allow her to depart!
10056{_}4430{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4431{_}Did I not think of her, I had a heart of iron--a     heart of iron!
10056{_}4432{_}The tears of my grief stream in thousand     channels--this evening shall her likeness be suspended in the     palace, where I will sacrifice to it--and tapers with their silver     lights shall illuminate her chamber.
10056{_}4433{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4434{_}Let your Majesty return to the palace--the princess     is already far distant!
10056{_}4435{_}[_Exeunt_.
10056{_}4436{_}_The Tartar Camp.
10056{_}4437{_}Enter K'han at the head of his tribes, leading in the Princess_.
10056{_}4438{_}K'HAN.
10056{_}4439{_}The Emperor of Han having now, in observance of     old treaties, yielded up to me the Lady Chaoukeun in marriage, I     take her as my rightful queen.
10056{_}4440{_}The two nations shall enjoy the     benefits of peace.
10056{_}4441{_}[_To his generals_] Leaders, transmit my     commands to the army to strike our encampment, and proceed to the     north.
10056{_}4442{_}[_They march_.
10056{_}4443{_}_The river Amoor.
10056{_}4444{_}[2] Tartar army on its march_.
10056{_}4445{_}PRINCESS.
10056{_}4446{_}What place is this?
10056{_}4447{_}ENVOY.
10056{_}4448{_}It is the River of the Black Dragon, the frontier of     the Tartar territories and those of China.
10056{_}4449{_}This southern shore is     the Emperor's; on the northern side commences our Tartar dominion.
10056{_}4450{_}PRINCESS [_to the K'han_].
10056{_}4451{_}Great King, I take a cup of wine,     and pour a libation towards the South--my last farewell to the     Emperor--[_pours the libation_] of Han, this life is finished.
10056{_}4452{_}I     await thee in the next!
10056{_}4453{_}[_Throws herself into the river.
10056{_}4454{_}The K'han, in great consternation, endeavors to save her, but in vain_.
10056{_}4455{_}K'HAN.
10056{_}4456{_}Alas!
10056{_}4457{_}alas!--so determined was her purpose against     this foreign alliance--she has thrown herself into the stream, and     perished!
10056{_}4458{_}Tis done, and remediless!
10056{_}4459{_}Let her sepulchre be on this     river's bank, and be it called "the verdant tomb," [3] She is no     more; and vain has been our enmity with the dynasty of Han!
10056{_}4460{_}The     traitor Maouyenshow was the author of all this misery.
10056{_}4461{_}[_To an     officer_] Take Maouyenshow and let him be delivered over to the     Emperor for punishment.
10056{_}4462{_}I will return to our former friendship with     the dynasty of Han.
10056{_}4463{_}We will renew and long preserve the sentiments     of relationship.
10056{_}4464{_}The traitor disfigured the portrait to injure     Chaoukeun--then deserted his sovereign, and stole over to me, whom     he prevailed on to demand the lady in marriage.
10056{_}4465{_}How little did I     think that she would thus precipitate herself into the stream, and     perish!--In vain did my spirit melt at the sight of her!
10056{_}4466{_}But if I     detained this profligate and traitorous rebel, he would certainly     prove to us a root of misfortune: it is better to deliver him for     his reward to the Emperor of Han, with whom I will renew, and long     retain, our old feelings of friendship and amity.
10056{_}4467{_}_[Exeunt._    [Footnote 1: It may be observed that the great wall is never once expressly mentioned through this drama.
10056{_}4468{_}The expression used is Peensih, the border, or frontier.
10056{_}4469{_}The wall had existed two hundred years at this time, but the real frontier was beyond it.]
10056{_}4470{_}[Footnote 2: Or Saghalien, which falls into the sea of Ochotsk.]
10056{_}4471{_}[Footnote 3: Said to exist now and to be green all the year.]
10056{_}4472{_}~ACT FOURTH~    _Enter Emperor, with an attendant_.
10056{_}4473{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4474{_}Since the princess was yielded to the Tartars, we     have not held an audience.
10056{_}4475{_}The lonely silence of night but increases     our melancholy!
10056{_}4476{_}We take the picture of that fair one and suspend it     here, as some small solace to our griefs, [_To the attendant_]     Keeper of the yellow gate, behold, the incense in yonder vase is     burnt out: hasten then to add some more.
10056{_}4477{_}Though we cannot see her,     we may at least retain this shadow; and, while life remains, betoken     our regard.
10056{_}4478{_}But oppressed and weary, we would fain take a little     repose.
10056{_}4479{_}[_Lies down to sleep.
10056{_}4480{_}The Princess appears before him in a vision_.]
10056{_}4481{_}[1]  PRINCESS.
10056{_}4482{_}Delivered over as a captive to appease the barbarians,     they would have conveyed me to their Northern country: but I took an     occasion to elude them and have escaped back.
10056{_}4483{_}Is not this the     Emperor, my sovereign?
10056{_}4484{_}Sir, behold me again restored.
10056{_}4485{_}[_A Tartar soldier appears in the vision_.]
10056{_}4486{_}SOLDIER.
10056{_}4487{_}While I chanced to sleep, the lady, our captive, has     made her escape, and returned home.
10056{_}4488{_}In eager pursuit of her, I have     reached the imperial palace.--Is not this she?
10056{_}4489{_}[_Carries her off.
10056{_}4490{_}The Emperor starts from his sleep_.]
10056{_}4491{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4492{_}We just saw the Princess returned--but alas, how     quickly has she vanished!
10056{_}4493{_}In bright day she answered not to our     call--but when morning dawned on our troubled sleep, a vision     presented her in this spot.
10056{_}4494{_}[_Hears the wild fowl's [2] cry_] Hark,     the passing fowl screamed twice or thrice!--Can it know there is no     one so desolate as I?
10056{_}4495{_}[_Cries repeated_] Perhaps worn out and weak,     hungry and emaciated, they bewail at once the broad nets of the     South and the tough bows of the North.
10056{_}4496{_}[_Cries repeated_] The     screams of those water-birds but increase our melancholy.
10056{_}4497{_}ATTENDANT.
10056{_}4498{_}Let your Majesty cease this sorrow, and have     some regard to your sacred [3] person.
10056{_}4499{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4500{_}My sorrows are beyond control.
10056{_}4501{_}Cease to upbraid     this excess of feeling, since ye are all subject to the same.
10056{_}4502{_}Yon     doleful cry is not the note of the swallow on the carved rafters,     nor the song of the variegated bird upon the blossoming tree.
10056{_}4503{_}The     princess has abandoned her home!
10056{_}4504{_}Know ye in what place she grieves,     listening like me to the screams of the wild bird?
10056{_}4505{_}_Enter President_.
10056{_}4506{_}PRESIDENT.
10056{_}4507{_}This day after the close of the morning council,     a foreign envoy appeared, bringing with him the fettered traitor     Maouyenshow.
10056{_}4508{_}He announces that the renegade, by deserting his     allegiance, led to the breach of truce, and occasioned all these     calamities.
10056{_}4509{_}The princess is no more!
10056{_}4510{_}and the K'han wishes for peace     and friendship between the two nations.
10056{_}4511{_}The envoy attends, with     reverence, your imperial decision.
10056{_}4512{_}EMPEROR.
10056{_}4513{_}Then strike off the traitor's head, and be it presented     as an offering to the shade of the princess!
10056{_}4514{_}Let a fit banquet be     got ready for the envoy, preparatory to his return.
10056{_}4515{_}_[Recites these     verses_.
10056{_}4516{_}At the fall of the leaf, when the wild-fowl's cry was heard       in the recesses of the palace.
10056{_}4517{_}Sad dreams returned to our lonely pillow; we thought of       her through the night: Her verdant tomb remains--but where shall we seek her       self?
10056{_}4518{_}The perfidious painter's head shall atone for the beauty       which he wronged.
10056{_}4519{_}[Footnote 1: There is nothing in this more extravagant than the similar vision in the tragedy of Richard III.]
10056{_}4520{_}[Footnote 2: Yengo, a species of wild goose, is the emblem in China of intersexual attachment and fidelity, being said never to pair again after the loss of its mate.
10056{_}4521{_}An image of it is worshipped by newly married couples.]
10056{_}4522{_}[Footnote 3: Literally, "dragon person."
10056{_}4523{_}The emperor's throne is often called the "dragon seat."]

10056{_}4645{_}EBooks posted prior to November 2003, with eBook numbers BELOW #10000, are filed in directories based on their release date.
10056{_}4646{_}If you want to download any of these eBooks directly, rather than using the regular search system you may utilize the following addresses and just download by the etext year.
10056{_}4647{_}http://www.ibiblio.org/gutenberg/etext06      (Or /etext 05, 04, 03, 02, 01, 00, 99,      98, 97, 96, 95, 94, 93, 92, 92, 91 or 90)  EBooks posted since November 2003, with etext numbers OVER #10000, are filed in a different way.
10056{_}4648{_}The year of a release date is no longer part of the directory path.
10056{_}4649{_}The path is based on the etext number (which is identical to the filename).
10056{_}4650{_}The path to the file is made up of single digits corresponding to all but the last digit in the filename.
10056{_}4651{_}For example an eBook of filename 10234 would be found at:       http://www.gutenberg.net/1/0/2/3/10234  or filename 24689 would be found at:      http://www.gutenberg.net/2/4/6/8/24689  An alternative method of locating eBooks:      http://www.gutenberg.net/GUTINDEX.ALL
